THE STORY OF THE INCARNATION AS KAPILA

_____

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ã‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡•á‡§¶‡•á ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡§∞‡§¶‡§æ‡§∂‡•Å‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Being told by (the Creator) Brahmato procreate human beings, the divine with devotion Kardama* sought with devotion (Lord) Hari who liberally bestows boons on those who seek Him.

‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§™‡•Å‡§É‡••

Becoming gracious (towards Kardama), the Lord showed him His ferm.

____________________________________________________________________________________________

* Kardama: The creator Brahma who was born of the navel-lotus of the Lord created the elements, the world of animals and trees and then the sages and divine beings. Among the last were Daksha, Kardama and others who were the progenitors of the human race (Prajapatis).

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî

‚Äò‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∂‡§§‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ü‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã‡••

The Lord‚Äî

“Great sage! the Emperor (Manu)*, the son of the Creator, will go (here) with his queen Satarupa and will give in marriage his daughter (Devahuti) to you who are a
meet husband for her.

‘‡§∏‡§π‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡§ï‡§≤‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡§µ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§π‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

“Great Sage, partially manifesting myself through your energy in thy wife Devahuti, I shall found a system of philosophy.”

____________________________________________________________________________________________

* Manu is the first man. After creating the sages and divine boings, Brahma felt that he could not yet bring into being the human species and as he was feeling thus, his form divided into two, a male and a female. The male is Manu, the first man and emperor; he is called Svayambhuva Manu, i.e., Manu born of the Creator, Svayambhu. The female was Satarupa who became Manu’s queen and from this prime-couple, the human species began to develop. Two sons, Priyavrata and Uttanapada, and three daughters, Akuti, Devahuti and Prasuti, were born to Manu and Satarupa. Manu gives Devahuti in marriage to Kardama Prajapati and of those two is born sage Kapila, an incarnation of the Lord to bless the world with spiritual enlightenment.

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•É‡§∑‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§¨‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§∏‡§∞‡§∏‡§ø ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•á‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡•§
‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§™‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§É‡••

Then, after the Lord (the pure Being) had disappeared, the divine sage Kardama was staying at (lake) Bindusaras, awaiting the time (of Manu’s arrival). (Manu,) the first of Kings, along with his daughter, came to (Kardama’s) hermitage.

‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§É‚Äî

‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§¶‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Å‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§£ ‡§Æ‡•á‡••’

Manu‚Äî

‚ÄúThis daughter of mine, the sister of Priyavrata and Uttanapada, seeks a suitable husband; accept her whom whom I give marriage to you.”

‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡§É‚Äî

‡§¨‡§æ‡§¢‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§¢‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§æ’‡••

Kardama‚Äî

“Surely I am desirous of marrying and your daughter has not yet been given in marriage to anybody.”

‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§´‡•Å‡§ü‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§ó‡§£‡§æ‡§¢‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§¶‡§¶‡•å ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

After learning clearly the resolve of his queen and of his daughter, Manu with great delight gave in marriage to the sage, who was rich with a multitude of virtues, his daughter who was equal to the sage in her qualities ).

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§•‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§∏‡•Ç‡§¶‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ã ‡§ú‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§Ω‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§ø‡••

After a long time, Lord Hari entered the energy of Kardama and was born of Devahuti, like fire of wood.

‡§∏ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§§‡••

And Kardama, understanding his son as God incarnate, spoke.

‘‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§™‡§ø‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á
‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§Ω‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç
‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡§É‡••

“I take refuge in Kapila whose power is dependent on Himself alone. I now take leave of you (Kapila), the Lord of all beings. Taking to the path of the Sannyasin, I shall move about, fixing you in my heart and bereft of all sorrow.‚Äù

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî

’ ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡§•‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§® ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ‡•§
‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The Lord‚Äî

“This secret path for realising the self has been lost for a long time. Know that this body has been taken by me to restore it.

‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ‡•§
‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ú‡••

“Go as you please; you are permitted by me; with your action offered up to Me, conquer the very invincible Death and seek Me for Immortality.

‘‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§Ü‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§Æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∏‡•å ‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••

‚ÄúI shall impart to my mother(also) the spiritual knowledge that puts an end to all action, whereby she too shall overcome Fear. "

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§π‡••

So told by Kapila, Kardama went away to the forests.

‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§∏‡§∞‡•á‡§Ω‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡§™‡§ø‡§≤‡§É ‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤‡••

On the retirement of His father to the forests, Lord Kapila, desiring to do what was dear to His mother, took His mother, took his abode near the lake Bindusara.

‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§π‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π ‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§§‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã‡•§
‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤‡•§
‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§Æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§á‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§Æ‡§™‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∏‡§ø‡••’

Devahuti told her son: “Lord, I am in the utter darkness (of nescience). You are that prime Being, the Lord and Master

of all men, risen like the sun who is the eye of this world, which is blinded with darkness. Therefore, O God! you must remove my gross ignorance.”

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî

‘‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó ‡§Ü‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ï‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§É‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§®‡•à‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The Lord‚Äî

‚ÄúThe Yoga of self-knowledge is considered by me as the means of attaining the eternal weal; and that yoga which is efficiency itself in every respect, I shall expound to you.

’ ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§É ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡•á‡••

“The mind it is that is held as the cause of the soul’s bondage as well as of its release; engrossed in material objects of enjoyment, it makes for bondage; if it revels in the spirit, it makes for emancipation.

’ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡§ú‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§™‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

“Attachment to evil, men of vision consider as the never‚Äîslackening bondage of the soul; the same attachment, if it is with the good souls, becomes the open entrance to deliverance.

‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§µ‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§É ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§µ‡§É ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∑‡§£‡§æ‡§É‡••

“Good men are they who are forbearing and and compassionate, who are friends to all beings and for whom there has never been any foe, who are mild and
for whom their character is the ornament.

‚Äò ‡§®‡•à‡§ï‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§π‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•á‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç
‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§π‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö
‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡•ã ‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúSome desire not oneness with Me, delighting as they do in service at My feet and yearning for Me,‚Äî those for whom I am the object of love, the soul, son, companion, teacher, friends and the deity beloved.

‘‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§µ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§É‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ã‡§¶‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡•Ä‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúOnly this much is the fulfilment of everlasting welfare in this world for men, namely, the firm offering of the mind to Me with intense devotion.

‘‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§∑ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡•§
‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§Æ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§π‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§É‡•§
‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§™‡§É ‡§∂‡•å‡§ö‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡§ö‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§è‡§§‡•à‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡§•‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§Æ‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç ‡••

“Performing one’s Dharma up to his capacity, turning away from what is another’s Dharma, contentment with what is one’s lot by destiny, worshipping the feet of men of self‚Äîrealisation, abstaining from doing the low and vulgar, and taking pleasure in the Dharma that would lead to liberation,

eating pure food in moderation, frequently resorting to the security of solitude, non-injury, truthfulness, non-stealing, taking no more than the necessary amount of material possession, restraint in sexual enjoyment, penance, personal purity, study of scriptures, worship of God,‚Äî by these and other ways mind casts off its impurity.

‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§æ‡•§
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡§É‡••

“He who who practises devotion to me, contemplating harm (to other beings), with pride and malice, ostentatious and seeing difference (everywhere), is one who is impelled by ignorance.

‘‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§∂ ‡§ê‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡§É‡••

“He who,contemplating objects of enjoyment, fame or riches, worships Me in images and the like‚Äîthat man who also has the sense of difference, is one who is prompted by passion.

‘‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡§ú‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§É‡••

“He who offers his worship to the Supreme with the object of doing away with both good and evil, or worships Him because he must, is one informed by knowledge, though he also has the sense of difference.

‘‡§Ö‡§π‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ‡•§
‡§§‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§°‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúI, the soul of all beings, am always present in all beings ; ignoring me mortal man performs who am there, this mortal the mockery of image‚Äîworship.

‘‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§Ç‡§≠‡§ú‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡•å‡§¢‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§ú‡•Å‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§É‡••

‚ÄúHe who leaves Me (who am) present as Soul and Master in all beings, and, in his stupidity, seeks an image, verily pours his offering on the ashes (and not in the fire).

‘‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§® ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø‡••

‚ÄúThe mind of that person who hates me in the bodies of others, is conceited, differentiates, and is inimical towards beings, does not attain peace.

‘‡§Ö‡§π‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§µ‡§ö‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§®‡§ò‡•á‡•§
‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡••

“O! Sinless (mother)!, I am not satisfied in the least if worshipped in my image, with the ritual begun with manifold paraphernalia, by him who insultsall beings.

‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúDoing his duty, one duty, one should Me, the Master, in images and the like only so long as he does not in his heart realise Me as established within all beings.

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡••

Therefore, one should honour with gifts and respect, with friendlineas and an eye which is not invidious, Me who, as the soul of all beings, have my temple in all beings.

‘‡§Æ‡§®‡•à‡§∏‡•à‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§ï‡§≤‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡••

“Honouring all these beings, one should bow to them with his mind, thinking that and Master has entered them the Lord and Master has all as the immanent spirit.

‚Äò‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§≠‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Æ‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§É‡••

‚Äú Bear in your heart these thoughts of mine which the expounders of the Supreme Spirit cherish; by these you shall attain Me who am birthless and those who know them not go to death.”

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§™‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å‡••

Showing thus His path to that virtuous woman, the Lord Kapila disappeared on being permitted by his mother who had spoken of matters of the Spirit with him.

‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡§®‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™ ‡§π‡••

And the mother, Devahuti also, by the path shown by her son, soon attained that Supreme Lord who is Himself one’s soul, the universal soul and the final beatitude.

‡••‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§™‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§•‡§æ‡••

______

THUS ENDS THE STORY OF THE INCARNATION AS KAPILA

__________

.‡••‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É‡••

‡••‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734617137Screenshot2024-12-17150708.png”/>

THE STORY OF DHRUVA

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734617176Screenshot2024-12-19151251.png”/>

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•å ‡§∂‡§§‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡•å‡•§
‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§≤‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•å‡••

Priyavrata and Uttanapada, the sons of Manu, the husband of Satarupa, imbued with an element of God Vasudeva, were engaged in protecting the world.

‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§§‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡•ã ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É‡••

** **There were two wives to Uttanapada, Suniti and Suruchi; of the two, Suruchi was the beloved of her lord, and not the other, whose son was Dhruva.

‡§è‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡•á‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§ï‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≤‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ω‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§§‡••

Once, taking Uttama, the son of Suruchi, on his lap and fondling him, the king did not like Dhruva who also desired to get on his lap.

‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É ‡§∏‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡••

As the king was listening, the exceedingly haughty Suruchi told Dhruva, her co-wife’s son, who was desiring to get upon the lap of his father:

‘‡§® ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§¢‡•Å‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§® ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§µ‡§™‡§ø ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ä‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§∏‡§ø ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡••’

“Child, you do not deserve to get upon the king’s throne; for, though the son of the king, you were not born of my womb. If you desire to be seated with the king contrive to be born of me.”

‡§≠‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã
‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó ‡§â‡§¶‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç
‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡§ï‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡••

Pierced by these very sharp words of his step-mother, Dhruva approached his own mother, weeping bitterly. Youthful Suniti took her boy on her lap, heard of what had taken place and told him:

‚Äò‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§§ ‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ
‡§≠‡•Å‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ú‡§®‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á
‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§â‡§¶‡§∞‡•á ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§∞‡§æ‡§ß‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ú‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ç
‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ä‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡••’

‚Äú Child, do not think ill of others; for man but reaps the misery he has caused to others. Suruchi hath spoken but truth ; for you have been borne in the womb of an unfortunate woman. Worship the desire the lotus-feet of God Hari if you desire high seat like Uttama. "

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§ï‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ö‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

Hearing his mother’s words thusblabbered (in grief), words which were (destined) to accomplish his object, Dhruva controlled his mind himself and went out of his father’s city.

‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ò‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

Hearing of that (Ceparture of Dhruva) and understanding what he desired to do, Narada (who met him) touched him on his head with his sin-destroying palm and wondering (at him), said:

‚Äò‡§®‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§®‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•§
‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å‡•§

“Child, to you who are yet a boy engrossed with your toys and the like, I do not see how any insult or honour is possible.

‘‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§® ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§∑‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§ú‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡••

‚ÄúThough there is the difference of insult and honour, there are (really) nocauses for discontent for a man except his ignorance; for, in (this) world, men aredifferent because of their own actions.

‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§ ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É‡•§
‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡§É‡••

“Therefore, dear child, the wiseman should content content himself with that which him, under-destiny has provided for him, standing the design of the Master.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á‡§® ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∏‡§ø‡•§
‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡••

“Further, He whose grace you desire to obtain through the Yoga taught by your mother, He, I consider, is hard to be propitiated by men.

’ ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∑ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§µ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§´‡§≤‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡••

“Therefore, may you turn back; this tenacity of thine is futile; thou is futile; thou shouldst make (all these) efforts when the propitious time comes.

‘‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§¶‡§®‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§ß‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§® ‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡•à‡§∞‡§≠‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••’

“A man should desire to be pleased with one who is superior to him in endowments; to be sympathetic to one who is inferior in endowments; and should seek friendliness with one who is equal in in endowments ; (doing thus), he is not heart-burnings.”

‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É‚Äî

‘‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§π‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§Ø‡§É‡••

Dhruva‚Äî

“This way of composing oneself has been kindly shown by your blessed self to men who are assailed with pleasure and pain, a path hardly perceivable by persons like myself.

‘‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ω‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ò‡•ã‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡•á‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∑‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ç‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡•ã‡§¨‡§æ‡§£‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§® ‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§ø‡••

" Still, (this advice of yours) does not enter (this) heart of mine that is pierced with the shafts of Surichi’s sharp words, this heart of myself who am unsubdued and violently militant in spirit.

‘‡§™‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ø‡§ó‡•Ä‡§∑‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡•§
‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••’

“(Therefore), O, Brahmin sage! tell the successful path to me who am desirous of winning that place which would be the highest in (all) the three worlds, a place which neither our ancestors nor others ever occupied.”

‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡§É‚Äî

‘‡§ú‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§®‡§ø‡§É‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•á‡•§

‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§ ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ü‡§Ç‡§∂‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡•§

‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡§∞‡•á‡§É‡•§

‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§µ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§

‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§ï‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§æ ‡§µ‡§∞‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§

‡§ú‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§ó‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡•§

‚Äú‡§ì‡§Ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡••”

Narada‚Äî

“The path which your mother told you of is for your salvation. Therefore, my child,may welfare attend you; go to the pure bankof the Yamuna, the forest of Madhuvanawhere there is the eternalpresence ofGod Hari. With a constant and onepointed mind you should meditate uponthe munificent Lord with a smile andlook of love. And prince, hearken to this greatest and (most) secret Mantra that must be meditated upon and repeated:‘Om,obeisance unto Lord Vasudeva’.”

“‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∞‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

So told, that child-prince, Dhruva, went round Narada, bowed to him and went to the sacred Madhuvana marked with the footprints of Lord Hari.

‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§∞‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§™‡§¶‡•à‡§ï‡•á‡§® ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•å ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§£‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§≤‡§É‡•§
‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡§Ç‡§™‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡••

According to sage Narada’s instruction, he attentively worshipped the Supreme Being. Contemplating the Brahman, he stood on one leg, motionless like the trunk of a tree. As he was holding his mind on the Brahman, the three worlds shook.

‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§ï‡§§‡•Ä‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ
‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ã‡§∂‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§´‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§ü‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•à‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø
‡§¨‡§π‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§¶‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡••

Suddenly losing sight of Him who was flashing like a lightning within the lotusbud of his heart, as a result of his intellect becoming keen by the keen by the fruition of the Yoga, Dhruva (opened his eyes) and saw Him standing outside in the same manner.

‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‚Äì
‡§Ö‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§§‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•É‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•á‡§¨‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§É
‡§ö‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§≠‡•Å‡§ú‡•à‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡§ø‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡••

With fear coming upon him on seeing the Lord, the boy (Dhruva) prostrated himself on the ground, throwing his body down like a stick, looking at Him intently as if he were drinking Him in with his eyes, appearing to kiss Him with his mouth and embrace Him with numerous arms.

‡§∏ ‡§§‡§Ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‚Äî
‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§®‡§æ
** ‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂ ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§™‡•ã‡§≤‡•á ‡••**

Lord Hari, who is established in his as well as all all others’ hearts, finding him desirous of speaking but innocent of speech, kindly touched on the on the cheek, with his conch which embodies the Vedas, the boy who was was (standing) with folded hands.

‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§¶‡•à‡§µ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§Ç
‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•É‡§£‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

Obtaining the power of speech at that very moment, Dhruva for whom God had already reserved a permanent place, sang of Him in his devotion:

’ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç
‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ñ‡§ø‡§≤‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ß‡§∞‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§£‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§§‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

“Obeisance unto you, the Lord and Supreme Being who holds within Him all powers and who, entering me, kindles to life with His power this speech of mine that was dormant, as also my hands, feet, ears, the senses of touch and the rest, and my very life-breaths.

‘‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ó‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π‡§Ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§™‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø
‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§®‡•Å‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§Æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§Ü‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡••’

“I seek refuge in Thee who art that from which, one after another, Learning and other manifold powers fall away arrested with their progress every time,‚Äî that Brahman, the source of the Universe, the One, the Endless, the First, that which is Bliss itself and is the Immutable.”

‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡§Æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡••

Thus extolled, the Lord said this then:

’ ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§ï‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡••

‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§∞‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Å ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

“Young prince ! I know what resolve there is in your heart; welfare unto you; O, you of excellent vow, I shall grant that (object of yours) to you, though it is hard to be attained, namely, that resplendent permanent place, auspicious (lad) ! which is not occupied by anybody else, and around which is set the wheel of the luminaries, the planets, stars and constellations.

‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡•Å ‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§∑‡§ü‡•ç‡§É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∂‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡§æ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ω‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•á‡§π‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á ‡§ó‡§§‡§É‡••’

“When, handing over the kingdom( to you), your father retires to the forests, you shall, upholding Dharma, protect the kingdom for thirty‚Äîsix thousand years, with your faculties unimpaired. And having enjoyed the rightful things with which you will be blessed, you shall think of me in the end; and then shall you go to my place, whence one returns not.”

‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§ß‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§∞‡•Å‡§°‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Even as the lad was looking on, God Hari departed to His abode. And the lad also, though he had attained what he had wished for, returned to the city, not very much pleased.

‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É‚Äî

‘‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•à‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§ö‡§ø‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§µ ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∑‡§ø‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§ó‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§≠‡§µ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡•á‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••”

(Dhruva said unto himself:) “This has been sought by me by me in vain, like medicine sought after life had departed. Having

propitiated by my penance the Soul of the universe who is hard to be pleased, I, this unfortunate self, begged of the destroyer of the misery of birth anddeath, that misery itself.

‘‘‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•å‡§¢‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡§§‡•§
‡§à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä‡§£‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§´‡§≤‡•Ä‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§ß‡§®‡§É‡••’

“Alas ! in my folly I have begged for honour of Himwho gives the sovereignty of the self, like the pauper who begged of the king as a result of his misfortune.’

‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡•å ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡•Ä‡§É‡••

Bowing at the feet of his father and welcomed by him with blessings, Dhruva, respected (by all) and foremost among the good, bent his head in reverence to his two mothers.

‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡§§‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§¨‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡••

Suruchi lifted that lad who had bowed at her feet, embraced him and in in a tone tremulous with tears said: “Live long. "

‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§£‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§®‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

To him whom Lord Hari hath favoured as a result of his of his virtues of universal friendliness and the rest, all beings bend low, even as waters turn of themselves towards the low-lying place.

‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§®‡§®‡•Ä ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§â‡§™‡§ó‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§¶‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§æ

And Suniti, his mother, embraced her son, dearer to her than her life, and feeling beatified by the touch of his limbs, cast her anguish away.

‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§™ ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§®‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ω‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§§‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§Ç [ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ] ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§É ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The royal sage Uttanapada, hearing of and himself seeing that most wonderful greatness of his son, and seeing also the consent of the subjects, made Dhruva,. beloved of the subjects, the lord of the Kingdom.

‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡§≤‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•É‡§∂‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Seeing himself very old, king Uttanapada, becoming detached, started out to the forests thinking of the way to self-realisation.

‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§ú‡§§ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§∂‡§Æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Dhruva propitiated with with sacrifices the Lord of the sacrifices; with devotion to (that) imperishable Being, he saw established in himself and inall beings only that all-pervading God.

‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§≤‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É‡••

The subjects looked on Dhruva,. endowed with such conduct, as their father

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§∏‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•Ç‡§°‡§æ‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§≤‡§É‡••

Thus spending a long time, Dhruva, for whom Lord Hari was the greatest resort, became (the pole‚Äîstar) which is like a pure crest‚Äîjewel to the three worlds2 which the Lord had promised him.”).

‡•• ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‡••

________

THUS ENDS THE STORY OF DHRUVA

_____________________________________________________________________________

‡••‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É‡••

‡••‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É‡••

THE STORY OF THE INCARNATION
AS KING PRITHU

________

‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∑‡•Å‡§µ‡•á ‡§ò‡•á‡§®‡§Æ‡•Å‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Sunitha, the wife of (king) Anga*, gave birth to the terrible Vena.

‡§∏ ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡§∂‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡••

As a boy, he was butchering boys who were playing, as one butchers. animals.

___________________________________________________________________

* After Dhruva, his eldest son Utkala having become desireless of kingdom, his next son Vatsara became king. Vatsara’s wife gave birth to six sons; the eldest of these, Pushparna begot six sons on his two wives. The last of these, Vyushta, had a son named Sarvatejas by his wife named Pushkarini. Of Sarvatejas and Akuti was born the Manu named Chakshus. Chakshusha Manu had twelve sons, the last of whom, Ulmuka begot six sons, the eldest of whom was Anga.

‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ñ‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§®‡•É‡§™ ‡§Ü‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É‡••

Seeing his son wicked, king Anga became very depressed in mind.

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§£‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡•ã ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç
‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ó‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Thus disgusted, king Anga went away from the palace abandoning the sleeping mother of Vena.

‡§≠‡•É‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§Æ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡§Æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§É‡••

The sages, Bhrigu and others, who have always the security of the world in view, anointed as King, Vena, who Vena, who was not acceptable to the subjects.

‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§® ‡§Ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≠‡•á‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ò‡•ã‡§∑‡•á‡§£ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§É‡••

Haughty and imagining himself great, he insulted the eminent. " Brahmins ! You should not perform sacrifices; you should not make any gifts; you should not offer any oblations anywhere.” Thus did he prohibit Dharma by the beat of drum everywhere.

‘‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã ‡§â‡§≠‡§Ø‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§≠‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§™‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É‡••

‡§Ö‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§ï‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§∑ ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§§‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§£‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ ‡§ñ‡§≤‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§ú‡§ø‡§ò‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡•á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§∂‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡••’

“Alas, from thieves and from the tyrant, from both the sides, is the world faced with great calamity, like a log of wood burning at both ends. Out of fear for anarchy, this undeserving Vena was made king and from him also has fear come now. How can there be welfare for the people? Vena is wicked by nature and he desires to destroy the subjects. Still we shall pacify him so that the sin of having made him king shall not attach to us.

‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ó‡•Ç‡§¢‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§â‡§™‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡••

Resolving thus, the sages approached Vena with their anger concealed, and told him, conciliating him with gentle words:

‘‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§∂‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§Æ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§µ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§§‡§ø‡••

“Let not that Dharma which is the welfare of your subjects disappear from you; when it disappears, the king falls down from his power.

‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•á ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§ú‡§®‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•á‡••’

“The Lord is pleased with that King in whose country and city, Oblessed king ! the Lord is worshipped by the people; and what is unattainable when that King of kings is pleased?”

‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡§É‚Äî

‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ ‡§¨‡§§ ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡•á ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§∏‡§§‡•á‡••

Vena-

“You are either childish or you imagine Dharma in what is Adharma,‚Äîyou who ignore the husband who maintains you and adore the clandestine lover.

‘‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§∂ ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§è‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§µ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§∞‡§∂‡§æ‡§™‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É‡•§
‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡•á ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§æ‡§É‡••’

" Vishnu, Brahma, Siva, Brahma, Siva, Indra, Vayu, Yama, Surya,‚Äîthese and other gods, who have it in their power to bless or curse, are present in the body of the king; the king is the embodiment of all gods. Therefore, without malice for me, you Brahmins, worship me with sacrifices and rites.”

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§ö‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§ß‡•Ç ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§¢‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§ú‡§ò‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•Å‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡§Ç ‡§π‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

Thus insulted by Vena, the sages grew angry; and with their anger mounting up, they struck down with the (fatal ) sound of ‘Hum’, Vena, (already) killed by his insulting the imperishable Lord.

‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§∞‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§É‡•§
‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§•‡•Å‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡••
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã‡§É ‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§É ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§Ω‡§®‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡••

Of the arms of of king Vena who died childless, the arms that were being churned by Brahmins, was born a couple: a partial manifestation of Lord Vishnu, Prithu by name, who was to be an emperor of and the imperishable Goddess Lakshmi, always devoted to Vishnu, was born after Prithu as Archis.

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∑‡•á‡§ï ‡§Ü‡§∞‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡••

Brahmins, the expounders of the Godhead, performed the coronation of that Prithu.

‡§è‡§∑ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•ã ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•á‡§§‡•Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

He was the most eminent among those who upheld Dharma; he made the world follow Dharma, guarded its bounds and chastised its enemies.

‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§É ‡§∂‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§Ü‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡••

Having the patience of Mother Earth, he was ever sympathetic to the beings in suffering.

‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø‡•§
‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡§•‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

Steadfast in Dharma, this Prithu punished not the innocent, even if he were the son of one who hated him (Prithu), and he punished even his own son, if if the son deserved punishment.

‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∑‡•Å ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§á‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡§É‡••

He revered others’ women as his mother, and his own wife, he loved as half of his own self. He was affectionate towards his subjects like a father and increased the happiness of his friends.

‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§≤‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§¶‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§É ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•ã‡§∞‡§ø‡§π ‡§®‡•à‡§µ‡•à‡§∑‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§®‡§æ‡••

King Prithu, son of Vena, made (the surface of) the earth almost even; and on it then, Prithu, who was God Himself, and who maintained his subjects like a father, created everywhere places of dwelling,‚Äî

villages, cities, towns, and various kinds of forts. Before Prithu, there never was on this earth this devising of cities, villages and the like.

‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∞‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú ‡§á‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡§∞‡§É‡••

Delighting the subjects with the pleasing qualities of his mind, speech and conduct, Prithu bore the name ‘Raja’¬π(the delighter of the people), as if he were another moon.

‡••‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§•‡§æ‡••

_________

THUS ENDS THE STORY OF THE INCARNATION AS KING PRITHU

_____________________________________________________________________

  1. Prithu was called Raja, having been king par excellence. Both the moon and the king are called Raja. Raja is derived from the root Ranj to please. The ideal king is thus one who pleases his subjects.

_________

‡••‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É‡••
‡••‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§®‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¨‡•ã‡§ß‡§ï‡§•‡§æ‡••

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734613579arpita.PNG”/>

THE STORY OF THE ENLIGHTENMENT OF PRACHINABARHIS

‡§¨‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ã ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ö [‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§π]‡••

Barhishat, the very blessed son of Havirdhana, became became king; king;¬π he was an expert in the texts on sacrifices, and also in the several paths of Yoga.

‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§®‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∂‡•à‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The whole surface of the earth which was converted by him, who was performing sacrifice upon sacrifice, into sacrificial hall, was strewn over with the sacred-grass laid eastward.

____________________________________________________________________

1.Prithu was succeeded by Vijitasva his son, who had the other name Antardhana. By Nabhasvati, a wife of his, Antardhana had the son Havirdhana. Havirdhana had six sons, the eldest of whom was Barhishat otherwise called Prachinabarhis, one of the Prajapatis, (primeval progenitors) and always engrossed in sacrificial rites.

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§®‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ç [‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É] ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¨‡•ã‡§ß‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡••

The compassionate Narada who knew the Truth of Self enlightened this Prachinabarhis whose mind was engrossed in sacrificial rites:

‡§≠‡•ã ‡§≠‡•ã ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡•á [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§™‡§∂‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•á‡•§
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ò‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ò‡•É‡§£‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§É‡••

“O, king ! behold (these ) animals, these multitudes of living beings, that you have, without pity or disgust, butchered by thousands in your sacrifice!

“‡§è‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à‡§∂‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§§‡§µ‡•§
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ï‡•Ç‡§ü‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§õ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§É‡••”

“Remembering the slaughter done by you, they are looking forward to your death when, with their fury shooting up, they will tear you up with their steel‚Äîhorns.

‘‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§® ‡§∏ ‡§Ü‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É‡••

‡§®‡•à‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§® ‡§á‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§ò‡••

‚ÄúAs a man carrying a heavy burden on his head bears it (now) on his shoulder, even so are all remedies. Action by itself can never be the final remedy for Actions; for both proceed from nescience; O sinless soul ! it is like a dream within a dream!

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡•§
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§¶‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•å‡••

‚ÄúIt is this procession of birth and death which causes the series of calamities for the Self, the (real) object to be realised by that has one; and the snapping of that chain of birth and death is by supreme devotion to the Master.

‚Äò‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•á ‡§ö ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúWhen the Lord who has been realised in one‚Äôs self blesses one, he casts away the mind that has rooted itself in the world and sacrificial scripture.

‚Äò‡§Ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§É‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã ‡§¨‡•É‡§π‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡•à‡§∑‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

‚ÄúStrewing the whole of this earth with blades of grass thrown eastward, you pride yourself with this huge slaughter of living beings and imagining that you have done the right thing, you know not that which is the greater Karma. That is Karma which pleases Lord Hari; that is knowledge which makes one think of Him.

‚Äò‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§≠‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§®‡•É‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§π‡••

‚ÄúHari is the soul of all beings, Himself the source (of all) and Master. His feet are the refuge wherefrom welfare (flows) for men in this world.

‚Äò‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§® ‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§ø‡•§
‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡••

‚ÄúBeing the soul, He is the most beloved (for us); from Him there is not even an atom of fear. He who knows this, is the man of wisdom; the man of wisdom is the great man; great man; he is verily, Lord Hari.‚Äù

‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡•ã ‡§π‡§Ç‡§∏‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ó‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

Blessed Narada, chief among God‚Äôs devotees, having explained the natur of the Universal and Individual Souls, took leave of Prachinabarhis and then went to the world of those who have realised their Self.

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§®‡§¨‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡•á‡•§
‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡§ó‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡§™‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Becoming a royal sage, Prachinabarhis directed his sons to live the householder‚Äôs life and protect the people and went away for penance to the hermitage of sage Kapila.

‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§ï‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ú‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

There, the heroic Prachinabarhis continuously adored the lotus-feet of Lord Hari, with mind concentrated and attachments all abandoned; and by this devotion, he attained the state of equality with Lord Hari.

‡••‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§®‡§¨‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¨‡•ã‡§ß‡§ï‡§•‡§æ‡••

_____

THUS ENDS THE STORY OF THE
ENLIGHTENMENT OF KING PRACHINABARHIS.

_____

‡•• ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É ‡••

‡•• ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ï‡§•‡§æ ‡••

_______

THE STORY OF PRIYAVRATA

_______

** ‡§∏ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ-‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§≤‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§è‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡§® ‡§®‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡•§**

That (other) son of the king (Manu), Priyavrata¬π, a very great devotee of the Lord, who had learnt the Truth by service at the feet of Narada, was called upon by his father (Manu) to protect the world, but for the sake of uninterrupted contemplation of Lord Vasudeva, (he) did not relish (that duty).

__________________________________________________________________

  1. Priyavrata was brother of Uttanapada, father of Dhruva. The mapping out of the globe into the seven oceans and seven continents is said to date from the time of this Priyavrata who is described as having gone round the world many times.

__________________________________________________________________

** ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§π ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡•ã‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§**

‚Äò‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç
‡§Ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§Ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§π‡§∑‡§ü‡•ç‡§∏‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø
‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Then the self-born God Brahma spoke to Priyavrata thus: ‚ÄúTo the unwary, there may be fear even in the forests; for he is (surrounded) by his six enemies, (Passion, Anger, Avarice, Delusion, Pride, and Malice); and to that wise man who has conquered his senses and has found joy in his self, wnat harm can household life do?‚Äù

‚Äò‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§¨‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡§∞‡•ã‡§ú‡§ï‡•ã‡§∂-
‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§∑‡§ü‡•ç‡§∏‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡•Å‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ-
‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡••

‚ÄúAnd you have resorted to the stronghold of the lotus-feet of Hari and conquered the six enemies. Abandoning attachment, enjoy here the joys extended to you by the Supreme Being and (thus) realise your essential nature.

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏ ‡§ú‡§ó‡§§‡•Ä‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•á‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ß‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§ ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø-‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ó‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§∞‡§§‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡§æ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§≤‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•§

Thus, at the wish of the Lord, king Priyavrata assumed active duty, and remaining unsullied as a result of the power of the ceaseless contemplation of the feet of Lord Hari, the Prime Being, he ruled the earth.

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§®‡•Å ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§∞‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§™‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§™‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§∂‡§É‡••

Who else but the Lord can do what Priyavrata accomplished, Priyavrata who determined the world marking out the rivers, mountains, forests and the rest, and the distinct boundaries of each continent, for the peace of beings?

‡•• ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ï‡§•‡§æ ‡••

_____

THUS ENDS THE STORY OF PRIYAVRATA.

_____

‡•• ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É‡••

‡•• ‡§ã‡§∑‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§•‡§æ‡••

THE STORY OF THE INCARNATION
AS RISHABHA

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734239944Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png”/>

** ‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§§‡•§**

Desirous of issue, Nabhi3, along withhis childless (queen) Merudevi, worshipped the Lord.

** ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡•á‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ‡§§‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•§**

Wishing to please Nabhi, and with the desire to enunciate the Dharmas, the Lord incarnated Himself in his (queen) Merudevi.

** ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ö‡•å‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§ã‡§∑‡§≠ ‡§á‡§§‡•Ä‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•§**

Because of His superior energy, thefather gave Him the name Rishabha.

** ‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡§® ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§® ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•§**

Nabhi installed his son (Rishabha) inthe (duty of) guarding the bounds ofDharma (i.e., made him king), and, alongwith Merudevi, attained in course of timethe Lord, through contemplation.

** ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§π ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•É‡§∑‡§≠‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•ã ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§ß‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§ú‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•§ ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡•ã ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§Ü‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡••**

The Lord Rishabhadeva, inculcating theDharmas of the householders, begota hundred sons equal to Himself on (hiswife) Jayanti; of whom the eldest was thegreat yogin, Bharata of most eminentqualities, after whom this country is calledBharata varsha.

‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•É‡§∑‡§≠‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§É ‡§ï‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§µ ‡§à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡•á‡§®‡•ã‡§™‡§∂‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ ‡§â‡§™‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§ø‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ø‡§∂‡§É‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡•á‡§® ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§É‡••

Though He was master of Himself, and by Himself permanently devoid of all evils and though He was God Himself who is (ever) in the enjoyment of the bliss unimpaired, the Lord, with the name of Rishabha, taught by his own example the Dharmas to those ignorant of them. Remaining equal towards all, subduel in passions, full of friendliness and sympathy, He ordained the world in domestic life leading to the acquisition of Dharma, material gains, fame, children, pleasure and (in the end) salvation also. For, whatever the great man does, that the world does after him.

** ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡•á‡§£ ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£ ‡§è‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•á ‡§® ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§® ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§•‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§® ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø‡•§**

When this country was being protected by Lord Rishabha, none coveted for himself anything from anybody in any manner.

** ‡§∏ ‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡§¶‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡§∏‡§≠‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§**

Lord Rishabha once addressed his sons in the assembly of the greatest of Brahmin sages and as the subjects were listening:

‚Äò‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡•ã ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§≠‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡•É‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á
‡§ï‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§°‡•ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡§™‡•ã ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç
‡§∂‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•å‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É‡••

‚ÄúThis body with which men have been in this world of human beings, does not deserve the miserable pleasures which are like those of the filtheating creatures. Sons ! this body deserves that divine penance, by which one’s mind gets purified, and through which, is obtained the permanent bliss of Self.

‚Äò‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á
‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É
‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§É ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•á‡••

‚ÄúThe adoration of the great is said to be the door to deliverance; and association with those associated with women, theentrance to darkness. Great men are they whose minds are in equanimity, who have attained tranquillity, who are free from anger, who are friends (to all) and who are good in nature.

‚Äò‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø ‡§®‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§É
‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§§ ‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§≤‡•á‡§∂‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•ã
‡§∞‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§® ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§¢‡§É‡••

‚ÄúThe world has itself lost sight of its welfare, this world which in its great avarice, yearns for material for material possessions; creating mutual animosity for the sake of a morsel of enjoyment, this deluded world realises not the unending misery (it causes to itself).

‚Äò‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§® ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç
‡§® ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ö‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ω‡§™‡•á‡§§‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§

‚ÄúHe will not be a teacher, nor he a leader, who will not save one from impending death.

‚Äò‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§µ‡§ö‡•ã‡§¶‡•É‡§ï‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø
‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§¨‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§£‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç
‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∂‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúThe fruit of the activity of mind, speech, eye and the other aculties is the offering of it to Me. Without this, this, man cannot escape the stupendous nescience which is verily the noose of death.‚Äù

‡§è‡§∑‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•É‡§∑‡§≠‡§æ‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§®‡§Ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡§£‡§ø-‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ú‡•§

Having thus instructed his sons, the Lord in the guise of Rishabha appointed Bharata, the eldest of his hundred sons, to the (task of) protecting the world and Himself departed renouncing everything.

‡•• ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ã‡§∑‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§•‡§æ ‡••

THUS ENDS THE STORY OF THE
INCARNATION AS RISHABHA
‚Äî‚Äî‚Äî‚Äî

‡•• ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É ‡••

‡•• ‡§ú‡§°‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‡••

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734241834Screenshot2024-12-15104407.png”/>
THE STORY OF JADABHARATA

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734241854Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png”/>

** ‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ú‡§®‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§Ø‡•á‡§Æ‡•á, ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ú‡§®‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•§**

Bharata married Panchajani and begot on her five sons, equal to himself.

‡§∏ ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§≤‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡•§ ‡§à‡§ú‡•á ‡§ö ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ã‡§§‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§µ‡§ö‡•à‡§É‡••

That king Bharata of extensive knowledge protected with great affection his subjects who were devoted to their respective duties. He worshipped the Lord also with manifold sacrifices.

** ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§§‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ß‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§®‡§Ø‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§≤‡§π‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•§**

(Having lived) thus, Bharata, at the end of ten million years, resolved that the time for the end of enjoyment had come, divided the possession (of the kingdom) he was enjoying among his sons and himself retired to the hermitage of (sage) Pulaha.

** ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§ ‡§Ü‡§∞‡§æ‡§ß‡§®‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§≠‡•É‡§§‡•ã‡§™‡§∂‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•§**

There (in that hermitage), he propitiated the Lord and gaining more and tranquillity, he attained supreme bliss.

‡§è‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ó‡•É‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ã‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡•§

Once, he was sitting for some time on the bank of a river uttering the sacred Mantra.

‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡•Ä ‡§™‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ú‡§≤‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∂‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ‡•§ ‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•á‡§™‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§® ‡§â‡§¶‡§ï‡•á‡§Ω‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§≠‡§Ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§â‡§¶‡§™‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡•§ ‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§æ

‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§µ‡§ß‡•Ç‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡§¨‡§æ‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•à‡§µ‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§â‡§∞‡•Å‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ó‡§≤‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§∏‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡••

There, at that time, a thirsty doe approached the river. When the doe was drinking water, there arose from the neighbourhood the roar of the king of beasts which terrified the whole world. Hearing that, the doe, timid by nature, jumped away, all of a all of a sudden, out of fear. And as that pregnant doe was jumping, the young one in her womb slipped out, as a result of her great fright, and fell into the stream.

** ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§µ‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§£‡§≠‡§Ø‡§ñ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§∏‡§§‡•Ä ‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§™‡§æ‡§§, ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•§**

In the agony due to the discharge of the young one, the jump and the fright, the doe fell down in a cave and, after a time, died.

** ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§£‡§ï‡•Å‡§£‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§£‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§∞‡§§ ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§™‡§¶‡§Æ‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡•§**

Seeing the pitiable young one of the doe being carried along by the flood, the royal sage, Bharata, rescued it in his sympathy and took it to his hermitage.

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§£‡§ï‡•Å‡§£‡§ï ‡§â‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§®‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡§∞‡§π‡§É ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ã‡§∑‡§£‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§®‡§≤‡§æ‡§≤‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§è‡§ï‡•à‡§ï‡§∂‡§É ‡§ï‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§£‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡§∞‡§µ‡•ã‡§¶‡§µ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡•§

Towards this little deer, Bharata formed the strong attachment that it was his own, and as a result of his daily nourishing it, protecting it (from wild beasts), fondling it, satisfying its wants and continuous thinking of it, all his austerities, one by one, became extinct in a few days.

** ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§Ü‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•§**

To that Bharata whose Yoga was thus destroyed by the obstacle (of the young deer), there came the inescapable time of death.

‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó ‡§è‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡•É‡§∂‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§≤‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§≤‡§π‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ‡••

Passing away with a mind mind absorbed in the deer only, he was born (again) as a deer. (But) even in that deer-body, he thought of the cause for his becoming a deer and repenting very much, left his mother-doe, and again returned to the Lord’s own realm, the hermitage of (sages) Pulastya and Pulaha.

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡§ø ‡§∂‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§∞‡§£‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§ó‡§£‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•§

There, he lived lived on dried leaves, grass and creepers, counting the time for the expiry of the Karma that caused him to be born as a deer and (then) left his deer-body.

** ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§µ‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§µ‡§∏‡•ã‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ú‡§æ ‡§¨‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ‡•Å‡§É, ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§•‡•Å‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§Ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§™‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§∞‡§Æ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§É‡••**

Then, there were born to an excellent Brahmin nine sons by one wife, and by the younger wife twins, a son and a

daughter. The male-child of the twins, they say, was the great devotee Bharata who had left the deer-body and had become a Brahmin in his last birth.

‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡§®‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§≠‡•É‡§∂‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§¶‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§≤‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§ ‡§ú‡§°‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§¨‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á‡§£ ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•§ ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡••

In that birth also, he was terribly afraid of attachment to his kith and kin and remembering, by God’s grace, the series of his previous births, he exhibited himself to the world as a man mad, insensate, blind, and deaf. With an uncovered body, he wandered about in cold, heat, storm and rain.

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡§≤‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§™‡§∂‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§≠‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡§®‡•Å‡§ö‡§∞‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§ø ‡§è‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§∂‡§®‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡§≤‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§™‡§£‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§™‡§∂‡•ã‡§∞‡§∏‡•É‡§ó‡§æ‡§∏‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§¶‡•á‡••

Then, on an occasion, a certain banditchief, desiring issue, decided to offer a human sacrifice to Goddess Bhadrakali. His followers bound Bharata with a rope in the night and brought him to the temple of Chandika (Bhadrakali). Then, the bandit who was officiating as the priest of the banditchief took the sword for propitiating the Goddess with the wine of the blood of that human offering.

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§É‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§≤‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§ö‡§æ‡§ü ‡§∏‡•à‡§µ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•Ä‡•§

Seeing that highly heinous act of those low men of passion and delusion, delighting in violence, namely, the bad impermissible become the killing of one who Brahman, one from whom enmity had completely departed and one who was a friend of all beings, the Goddess Herself suddenly burst out of the image.

** ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§ü‡•ç‡§ü‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§ï‡•ç‡§£‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•É‡§ó‡§æ‡§∏‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡•Ä‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§ó‡•å ‡§®‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§§ ‡§ö‡•§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§¶‡§≠‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•á ‡§´‡§≤‡§§‡§ø‡••**

Laughing a terrific laugh, she jumped and with the same sword cut off the heads of those evil men, drank the wine of their blood, and sang, and danced. Thus indeed does the sin of torturing the great completely turnagainst the sinner (himself).

‡§® ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§¶‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§∏‡§Ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§¶‡§® ‡§Ü‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ-‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•É‡§¢‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§

Nor is this composure even when one’s decapitation is imminent any great wonder in those who have cast away that strong knot of the heart, the mistaken sense of soul in body and other material objects.

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§∏‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§∏‡•å‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§™‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ç‡§ó‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§§ ‡§á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ü‡•á ‡§∂‡§ø‡§¨‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§£‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§∏ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§µ‡§∞

‡§â‡§™‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§™‡•Ä‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ã‡§¢‡•Å‡§Æ‡§≤‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§π ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§≠‡§Æ‡§§‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§π ‡§∂‡§ø‡§¨‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§É‡•§

Then, while Rahugana, king of the Sindhus and the Sauviras, was on a journey along the bank of the Ikshumati, and a search was made for palanquin‚Äìbearers, this eminent Brahmin, Jadabharata, was found. ‚ÄúStout and youthful, this man is capable of bearing the burden‚Äù‚Äîthus was he forcibly caught hold of, along with others previously conscribed, and that great man undeservingly carried the palanquin.

‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§® ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§É, ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Æ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§ø‡§¨‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ç‡§ó‡§£ ‡§â‡§™‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡•§

When the movement of the bearers was not uniform, Rahugana found his palanquin moving irregularly and said: ‚ÄúWhy is the vehicle carried unevenly?‚Äù
‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡§É‚Äî

** ‚Äò‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§∞‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§® ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§§‡§ø, ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§π ‡§µ‡•ã‡§¢‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡•§‚Äô**

(The bearers said:) ‚ÄúKing, we are carrying (the palanquin) aright but this recently recruited person does not proceed fast and we are not able to carry it along with him.‚Äù

‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§∞‡§π‡•Å‡§ó‡§£ ‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§à‡§∑‡§¶‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‚Äî

King Rahugana, though he was one who had sat at the feet of the great, became a little angry and with mind sullied thereby, told Bharata whose Brahminic effulgence was not apparent:

** ‚Äò‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã ‡§ï‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§É! ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã,‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ò‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï ‡§è‡§µ ‡§ä‡§π‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡•Ä‡§µ‡§æ, ‡§® ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§π‡§®‡§®‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã, ‡§ú‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ö‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç !‚Äô**

‚ÄúAlas brother, what a misery! Clearly, you are very tired! Singly and for long, you have been carrying (the palanquin) a long way! You are not very stout or sturdy in limbs and you are decrepit !‚Äù
