‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§ø‡§¨‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§¶‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•§

Though scolded ironically in this manner, Bharata, who had become the Brahran, silently bore the palanquin as before.

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•Å‡§™‡§ø‡§§ ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡§∞‡§π‡•Ç‡§ó‡§£‡§É ‚Äò‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•É‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§ö‡§∞‡§∏‡§ø, ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§ö‡§ø‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‚Äô ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡•§

Then Rahugana, becoming very angry, told him: ‚ÄúWhy do you disobey the order of the master? I will give the (proper) remedy (of punishment) to you who are negligent.‚Äù

‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§®‡§∞‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§É‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§® ‡§á‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•§

That blessed Brahmin, who had become the Brahman and whose soul had become the friend of all beings, said this with a smile to that Rahugana who was prattling in that manner and was proud of being a king:

‚Äò‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•å‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§ß‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•É‡§°‡•ç‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§≤‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ ‡§ú‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ö‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡§π‡§Ç‡§Æ‡§¶‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡•Å‡§ö‡•ã
‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡•á‡§® ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§® ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡•§

Stoutness, leanness, physical ills, mental anguish, the fear of hunger and thirst, quarrel, desire, old age, sleep, enjoyment, anger, the intoxicating sense of I, sorrows,‚Äïthese exist for him who is born in the flesh, not for me (who am born in spirit).

‚Äò‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ ‡§à‡§°‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞
‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡•å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§É‡••

‚ÄúO praiseworthy king! if the relation of servant and master is eternal, then there shall be this relation betweenorder and service.

‚Äò‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç ‡§ö
‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï ‡§á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç
‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á‡••

‚ÄúExcept in words, we do not see any occasion for the sense of difference (of master and servant). When the fact is such, who is the lord and what is there to be lorded over? Still, O king, what shall we do for you?

‚Äò‡§â‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ú‡§°‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ç
‡§ó‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§∂‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§®
‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§™‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§™‡•á‡§∑‡§É‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúO heroic king! of what avail is the remedy of your punishment to me who, though looking like one mad, intoxicated or insensate, am really one who has attained selfhood? And if I were really stupid or mad, your punishment would be (all the more ) futile.‚Äù

‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞ ‡§â‡§™‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡§® ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡•§

Having replied this much, that eminent sage, who was living out the fruits of those past actions which had begun to
bear fruit, carried the royal vehicle.

‡§∏ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ö‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§µ‡§ö ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø, ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§µ‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§∏‡•É‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡§§‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§

And Rahugana, on hearing those words of the eminent Brahmin which cut the knot of nescience, got down (from his

palanquin) in haste, bowed at his feet, and with his pride of kingship gone, begged pardon of him and said:

‚Äò‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡•Ç‡§¢‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§∏‡•Ä‡§π ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•á‡§¶‡§∏‡§ø ‡§®‡•ã‡§§ ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§π‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúWho are you that move about here in disguise, and wherefore? If you are here for my welfare, may you not be the pure Lord Himself? I am on my way to enquire (what my refuge is) of Kapila, the first preceptor of all sages. May it be that thou art Himself?

‚Äò‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∞‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®-
‡§Æ‡§¶‡•á‡§® ‡§§‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•Ä‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü ‡§Æ‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã
‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§§‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡§¶‡§µ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§π‡§É‡••

‚ÄúTherefore, O, you friend of the suffering, you must grace with a look of friendliness me who have, in the intoxication of my pride of kingship, slighted the noblest of men; so only may I escape escape the sin of insulting the good.‚Äù

** ‡§ú‡§°‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§É‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§É
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§®‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§•‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

** Jadabharata‚Äî **

‚ÄúAttached to material objects of enjoyment, the mind of beings makes for their misery, but if it is freed of such objects, it makes for welfare.

‚Äò‡§® ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡•É‡§®‡§∞‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞
‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡•Ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§®‡•ã‡§¶‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã ‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§∑‡§ü‡•ç‡§∏‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•ã
‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§π ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡•§

‡§® ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§® ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§µ‡§™‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡••

‚ÄúKing! so long as man does not shake off this nescience as a result of the rise of knowledge, and leaving off (all) attachments and conquering the six enemies (Desire, Anger, Avarice, Delusion, Pride and Malice), does not realise the Truth of Self, so long as he does not understand this

mind which conditions the (unconditioned) soul as the soil that produces the agonies of births and deaths of man, so long does man wander here (in the world of birth and death).

‚Äò‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡§¶‡§¶‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§â‡§™‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§ß‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∞‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã
‡§ú‡§π‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≤‡•Ä‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúTherefore, lay aside your carelessness, and with the sword of the worship at the feet of your preceptor and the Lord, slay this very powerful enemy of yours, which has grown powerful by (sheer) negligence, this mind which is unreal in itself but has deprived you of your soul.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ö‡§≤‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç
‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§µ ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•ã‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡§ß‡§ø‡§ó‡•Å‡§≤‡•ç‡§´‡§ú‡§ô‡•ç‡§ò‡§æ-
‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•Ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§É‡••

‚ÄúKing! this something of earth, if it moves about in the world for some reason, comes to

be known as man; and to that earthen form, there are, above its feet, the ankles, the shanks, the thighs, the hip, the chest, the neck and the shoulders.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§∏‡•á‡§Ω‡§ß‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§∂‡§ø‡§¨‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç
‡§∏‡•å‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂ ‡§Ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§¢‡§®‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∏‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§É‡••

‚ÄúAnd on the shoulder, there is is the wooden palanquin and in it there is the name ‚ÄòKing of the Sauviras‚Äô; and with the sense of mine grown strong in that name, you imagine yourself to be the king of the Sindhus and become blinded by that false pride.

‚Äò‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ-
‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø‡•§
‡§ú‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã
‡§® ‡§∂‡•ã‡§≠‡§∏‡•á ‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡§≠‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å ‡§ß‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§É‡••

‚ÄúForcibly conscribing these pitiable people rendered miserable by the great toil (of carrying you ), you are indeed merciless.

Boasting that you are the protector of the people, you, who are audacious, do not shine in the assemblies of the learned.

‚Äò‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§Ç
‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§∏‡§ó‡§£‡•à‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡§æ ‡§® ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø
‡§® ‡§ö‡•á‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§£‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡•§
‡§® ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∏‡§æ ‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§ú‡§≤‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§É
‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§∞‡§ú‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§∑‡•á‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúPure knowledge is the one Truth, and that, the men of vision say, is Lord Vasudeva. Rahugana, this man does not attain to by penance, sacrificial rite, libation, or household life; not by recitation of the Veda, never by worship of Water, Fire or Sun. It cannot be attained except by bathing oneself in the dust of the feet of the great.

‚Äò‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§∏‡•Å‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ú‡§æ‡§§-
‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§®‡•á‡§π‡•à‡§µ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§ï‡•ç‡§£‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§É‡•§
‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§¶‡•Ä‡§π‡§æ‡§ï‡§•‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç
‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§É‡••

‚ÄúTherefore cutting here itself his delusion with the sword of knowledge born of the association with those who have no attachments, and acquiring the constant thought (of the Lord) by speaking of and listening to His acts, acts, man reaches Hari, crossing the end of the road of this world.

‚Äò‡§∞‡§π‡•Ç‡§ó‡§£ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø
‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∏‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç
‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúRahugana, laying aside aside the role of punishing (others) and making friends with all beings, with your soul untouched by (objects of enjoyment) and arming yourself with the sword of knowledge, sharp with the service of Lord Hari, you also cross over the other end of this highway.‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§™‡§§‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§ø‡§ï‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§â‡§™‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§µ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§®‡§ø‡§≠‡•É‡§§‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ß‡§∞‡§£‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•§

Having thus, out of his great compassion, imparted the Truth of Self to the king of the Sindhus, Jadabharata wandered over this earth, looking like the full ocean, the waves of action in his mind having become still.

** ‡§∏‡•å‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§™‡§ø ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§É‡•§**
And the king of the Sauviras also cast away the sense of soul in the body, which has been superimposed on the self by nescience. Such is the greatness of those that resort to God’s devotees.

‡•• ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ú‡§°‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡••

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734278695Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png”/>
THUS ENDS THE STORY OF
JADABHARATA.

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734278695Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png”/>

‡•• ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É‡••

‡••‡§Ö‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734278784Screenshot2024-12-15104407.png”/>
THE STORY OF AJAMILA

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734278808Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png”/>

‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‚Äî

‚Äò‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∂‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§•‡•ã ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

**King Parikshit‚Äî **

‚ÄúThough knowing sin to be harmful to oneself from (both) the visible (society,elders and state) and the ethical Institutes one learns, one ( still) commits sin, unable to control oneself; and of what avail are expiatory rites then ?‚Äù

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡§É‚Äî

‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§® ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï ‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Suka‚Äî

The annihilation of sin by expiatory rites is not considered as final; for the expiatory rites are prescribed for those who are notmen of knowledge. Knowledge is expiation.

‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡§ø‡•§
‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ï‡•É‡§¶‡•ç [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§∂‡§®‡•à‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•á‡••

Diseases assail not him who eats only wholesome food; even so, the person of disciplined life gradually qualifies himself for ( ultimate) welfare.

‡§ï‡•á‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ò‡§Ç ‡§ß‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§®‡•Ä‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡§É‡••

Even as the sun dispels the fog, some solely devoted to Vasudeva shake off their sin completely by their devotion alone.

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§® ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞] ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡§ó‡§æ‡§É‡••

Even as all the rivers cannot sanctify a pot of liquor, all the expiatory rites do not make holy the holy the person who is averse to Narayana.

‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ö‡•ã‡§¶‡§æ‡§π‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Å‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§É [‡§§‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§¨‡•ã‡§ß ‡§Æ‡•á]‡••

And on this subject they tell an old story also, a conversation between the messengers of God Vishnu and Yama (the God of Death):

‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•Å‡§¨‡•ç‡§ú‡•á ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§É ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§æ ‡§®‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

There was a Brahmin in Kanyakubja, Ajamila by name, the husband of a prostitute, with all his righteous conduct lost and polluted by association with the harlot.

‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ï‡•à‡§§‡§µ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§¨‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§Æ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡••

Adopting despicable means of livelihood, sycophancy, gambling and theft, and maintaining his family impurely, that Ajamila was torturing people.

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§Ø‡§∏‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¶‡§∂ ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ‡§Æ‡§É‡•§
‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡•ã‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡•É‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•á ‡§ú‡§∞‡§†‡•ã ‡§≠‡•É‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

To him, who had become very old, there were (born) ten sons, of whom the last was a boy named Narayana, a darling of the parents. Doting on that child, the old man was extremely happy.

‡§∏ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§â‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§§‡§®‡§Ø‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡•á‡••

Living in this manner, the ignorant Ajamila, when the time of death approached, fixed his mind on that young son of his named Narayana.

‡§∏ ‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§≠‡•É‡§∂‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§®‡§ï‡§æ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•Å‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É‡••

Seeing three terrific persons with nooses in their hands, Ajamila, with his senses bewildered, called out in a long-drawn voice for his son named Narayana who who was engrossed in his dolls at a distance.

‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§≠‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ [‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú] ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§™‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡••

Hearing the name of their Lord from that dying person who was uttering the name of Hari, the attendants of the Lord rushed (to him) in haste.

‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Å‡§¶‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ‡••

The messengers of Vishnu forcibly prevented the servants of Yama who were dragging from out of the heart, (the soul of) Ajamila, the husband of the prostitute.

‡§ä‡§ö‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•á‡§ß‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡•à‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§æ‡§É‡••

Those forerunners of Yama, who were obstructed, told the messengers of Vishnu:

‚Äò‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§Æ‡••

‚ÄúDharma is that which is inculcated by the Veda; its opposite is Adharma; and we have heard that the Veda is the self-born God Narayana Himself.

‚Äò‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡•á‡§® ‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§É‡••

‚ÄúAll those who commit sin deserve punishment in accordance with what they have done.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§É ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§≤‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§è‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•å ‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§ï‡•É‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§É‡•§

‚Äò‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§π ‡§≠‡•Å‡§ú‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡••

‚ÄúThis person (Ajamila) was a Brahmin, endowed with learning and the abode of character, conduct and other virtues; once, having gone to the forest to do the bidding of his father, he saw a lewd low-caste fellow in the company of a harlot, dallying, singing and laughing with her who was by his side.

‚Äò‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§π‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•à‡§µ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

‚ÄúSeeing her embraced by that lustful person with his arm, this Ajamila became infatuated at once once and a prey to passion.

‚Äò‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§π‡•§
‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§§‡•ã‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á‡§® ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡••

‚ÄúThinking of her alone, he stopped performing his Dharma; and with all his available patrimony, he satisfied her alone.

‚Äò‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•å‡§¢‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡§ø ‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ß‡•Ä‡§É‡••

‚ÄúWith his mind pierced by the side-long glances of the wanton woman, the sinner, Ajamila, soon abandoned his own wife, a Brahmin lady, not yet of age, and married out of a great family.

‚Äò‡§Ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§™‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§ß‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¨‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúHe brought money justly or unjustly and from any kind of source and (with that), the fool maintained the family of that (harlot), who had a large family.

‚Äò‡§Ø‡§¶‡§∏‡•å ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§ô‡•ç‡§ò‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Æ‡§ò‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡§∂‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••
‡§§‡§§ ‡§è‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•á‡§É ‡§∏‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤‡•ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§®‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•á‡§® ‡§∂‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúSince this Ajamila, trangressing the sacred Institutes, licentious and contemned by the noble, has for a long a long time been leading a life of sin and has been impure with pollution, we we shall lead this sinner who has performed no expiation, to the presence of the dispenser of justice (Yama), where he he would become purified by punishment.‚Äù

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Å‡§¶‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡•ã ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ã‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§π‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø‡•§
‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∂‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§®‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∞‡•á‡§É‡••

The Lord’s messengers‚Äî

‚ÄúThis Ajamila has done the expiation for even the sins of a crore of births, since involuntarily he spoke the name of Hari, the path to welfare.

‚Äò‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ò‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

‚ÄúThis is the greatest expiation for all sinners, the uttering of the name of Vishnu whereby the thought of Him is produced.

‚Äò‡§∏‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§≠‡§Ç ‡§π‡•á‡§≤‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§æ‡•§
‡§µ‡•à‡§ï‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§Æ‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§ò‡§π‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡••

‚ÄúThe sages sages consider the mention of a name of Hari as destroying sin completely, even though the mention is due to the name being associated with something else4, or is done in jest, or is the result of involuntary sounds, or is done in derision.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§•‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§ò‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ã ‡§¶‡§π‡•á‡§¶‡•á‡§ß‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§®‡§≤‡§É‡••
‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ó‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡§æ‡§π‡•É‡§§‡§É‡••

‚ÄúThe name of God uttered consciously or unconsciously will burn away the sin of man, even as fire would burn fuel. Like very effective medicine taken in accidentally, a Mantra uttered does its good even to him who knows not its effect.

‚Äò‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç‡§µ‡§É ‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§ ‡§≠‡§ü‡§æ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúServants (of Yama ) ! if you haveany doubt in this Dharma, ask of your Master. He, Lord Yama, knows the greatest secrets of Dharma.‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Thus spoken to, the messengers of Yama went to Yama’s presence.

‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§ó‡§§‡§≠‡•Ä‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∂‡•Å ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§£‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•á‡§É‡••

Released from the noose (of death), the Brahmin, with his fear gone, regained his normal state and as a result of listening to the greatness of the Lord (from his messengers), quickly became a devotee of God.

‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∂‡•Å‡§≠‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‚Äò‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§¶‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡••
‡§ß‡§ø‡§ô‡•ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§ï‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§§ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡§§‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••
‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡§•‡•å ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡•å ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ç ‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•å‡•§
‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ß‡•Å‡§®‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§® ‡§®‡•Ä‡§ö‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡••

Recapitulating his sins, he repented intensely: Alas! What a great misery there was for me who had no self-possession and had destroyed my Brahminic line by begetting (children) on a low-caste woman! Fie upon me, accursed by the good, the sinner and blot on my family, who abandoned a young and faithful wife and went over to the drunkard-harlot! Alas! ungratefully and like a low person, I have now neglected my poor parents, who are old, helpless and have no kin besides myself!

‚Äò‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡§Ü‡§π‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§• ‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§æ‡§É‡••

‚ÄúIs this a dream or did I see here a wonder with my own eyes? Where have they gone now, they who dragged me with nooses in their hands? And] where have they gone, those four angels of beautiful appearance?

‚Äò‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§§‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§≤‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§® ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§§‡§Æ‡§∏‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡•á‡••

‚ÄúControlling my mind, senses, and breath, I will strive in such a manner as not to sink myself again in stark nescience.‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§∑‡•Å‡•§
‡§ó‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡§É‡••

Thus, with complete disgust for worldly enjoyment, born in him as a result of a moment’s association with the good, Ajamila came to the head of the Ganges, casting away all attachments.

‡§∏ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∏‡§¶‡§® ‡§Ü‡§∏‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§π‡•à‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

In that divine region he sat and took to Yoga; immediately he assumed the form of those who remain by the side of the Lord and, mounting a golden heavenly vehicle, reached the Lord’s abode.

‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•à‡§É [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§π‡§§‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The servants of Yama whose efforts were set at naught by the servants of the Lord, submitted to their master Yama, the lord of Samyamini (the city of justice)‡§É

‚Äò‡§ï‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§π ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã‡•§
‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§´‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§µ‡§É‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúMaster! how many masters are there for this world of living beings that is doing the threefold actions, meritorious, sinful and mixed,‚Äîmasters responsible for bringing about the fruits of these actions?‚Äù
‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§™‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ú‡§ó‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•Å‡§∑‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö
‡§ì‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§ü‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§¨‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§ ‡§á‡§Æ‡•á ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ-
‡§®‡§ø‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡••

Yama‚Äî

‚ÄúBesides me, there is a master for (this world of) moving and static objects, a master who is the warp and woof of the fabric of the universe, the master to whom these (gods), bound with the bonds of (definite) names and duties, bear in fear their offering of service.

‚Äò‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§™‡•Ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø
‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡•Ä‡§§‡§Ç
‡§® ‡§µ‡•à ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ã‡§∑‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§É‡••

‚ÄúThe angels of (that Lord) Vishnu, honoured by all gods, protect the devotees of that Lord from others; and Dharma, which is founded verily by the Lord Himself, neither the sages nor the gods comprehend.

‚Äò‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§µ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡••

‚ÄúOnly this much is considered as the greatest Dharma of men, namely, the practice of devotion devotion to the Lord by uttering his name and such other means.

‚Äò‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∞‡•á‡§É ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡§æ‡§¶‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡••

‚ÄúMy dear men! behold the greatness of the mention of Lord Hari’s name, by which alone even Ajamila was released from the noose of death.

‚Äò‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§™‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡§æ‡§•‡§æ
‡§Ø‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§∂‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡§§ ‡§π‡§∞‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§ó‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç
‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§∏‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Å‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúThey who are good, uninvidious and absolutely devoted to the Lord are those whose pure lays the divine beings sing. Them, protected by the mace of Hari, approach not. (But), bring me those bad men who did not do the service of Lord Vishnu.‚Äù

‡•• ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡••

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734324958Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png”/>
THUS ENDS THE STORY OF AJAMILA.

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734324958Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

‡•• ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É ‡••
‡•• ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§µ‡§ß‡§ï‡§•‡§æ ‡••

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734325033Screenshot2024-12-15104407.png"/>
THE STORY OF THE KILLING OF
VRITRA ASURA

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734324958Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ã‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§ô‡•ç‡§ò‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§•‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§§ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§®‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Transgressing the righteous path in the pride of the sovereignty of the three worlds, Indra (once) failed to rise, offer a seat and do similar honour to the eminent sage Vachaspati, revered by both gods and demons, on his arrival.

‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§¶‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¨‡•É‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§µ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

Going out of Indra‚Äôs court all of a sudden, and knowing as he did the evil effect of the pride of prosperity, Brihaspati became invisible by his spiritual power.

‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•å‡§∂‡§®‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¶‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§§‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡••

As soon as they heard of that disappearance of the preceptor of the gods, the maddened demons resorted to the advice of (their preceptor) Sukra and, determined to kill the gods, attacked them.

‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§®‡§§‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡••

With heads bent in reverence, the gods, with Indra, sought refuge in Brahma. God Brahma consoled the gods who were put to severe distress in that manner and told them:

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã ‡§¨‡§§ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§§‡••

‚ÄúAlas! you eminent gods! a great wrong has been committed by you, you who in your power did not honour the Brahmin (Brihaspati), a person of self-realisation and self-control.

‚Äò‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ú‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•Å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç
‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§•‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§≠‡§æ‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡•ã
‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúTherefore, quick, seek seek the Brahmin Visvarupa, a man of penance and self- possession, the son of Tvashta. Honoured (by you), he will do for you the things (you want), if only you tolerate his action (his partiality for the demons).‚Äù

‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡§Æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡••

So told, the gods approached Visvarupa, the son of Tvashta, and said this:

‚Äò‡§µ‡•É‡§£‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§π‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§µ ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúWe beseech you, you, a Brahmin of selfrealisation and one fit to be a preceptor, to become our preceptor so that, with your power, we shall conquer our enemies with ease.‚Äù

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§É
‡§™‡•å‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§π‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

Visvarupa‚Äî

‚ÄúMasters! how shall I undertake priestcraft, a despicable act which only a low mind delights in?

‚Äò‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•à‡§∞‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§Ø‡•á‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúStill, I shall accomplish (for you), with all my life and resources, all that you have requested (of me).‚Äù

‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡§™‡§æ‡§É ‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•å‡§∂‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ü‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§µ‡•à‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§É‡••

Having thus promised to the gods, the powerful Visvarupa of great penance snatched and gave to Indra, by (the power)

of the Mantra of Lord Vishnu, the fortune of the enemies of the gods, though it was
protected by the power of Sukra’s magic-lore.

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§ø [‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§]‡•§
‡§∏‡§µ‡•à ‡§¨‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§µ‡§¶‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡•ã ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ç [‡§®‡•É‡§™]‡••
‡§∏ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§¶‡§¶‡•å ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ‡§π‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§µ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡§É‡••

That Visvarupa had three heads.In his sacrifice, he pronounced loudly, in sight of all and with modesty, the share of the offering due to the gods, who were his kin on his father’s side; and the same person gave the demons their share, secretly; performing his sacrifice, Visvarupa gave their share (to the demons), impelled by his love for his mother.*

‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§π‡•á‡§≤‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡•Ä‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§ø‡§®‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡•§

___________________________________________________________________________

* Aditi, a wife of Kasyapa, produced many sons, one of whom was Tvashta. Tvashta married Racana, the sister of a demon and of the two was Visvarupa born. Thus, through his father, Visvarupa is a grandson of the gods and through his mother, a nephew of the demons.

___________________________________________________________________________

Seeing that insult of the gods and pretended Dharma of Visvarupa, Indra, the king of the gods, afraid (of Visvarupa’s attachment to the demons) quickly cut offhis heads in anger.

‡§π‡§§‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ ‡§ú‡•Å‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•á‡•§
‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§ö‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§ò‡•ã‡§∞‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§É‡••

Then, Tvashta whose son (Visvarupa) had been killed, made offerings in fire to create an enemy of Indra. And then, there arose out of the fire at the southern end, a terrible being; that very frightful evil spirit was called Vritra.

‡§§‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§ú‡§ò‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡§≠‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§ó‡§£‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•å‡§ò‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§∂‡§É‡••

The great gods attacked Vritra with their followers and struck him with their respective divine missiles and weapons. And Vritra swallowed them completely.

‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§ ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡••

Then the gods praised the Prime Being with concentrated minds.

‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π ‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§ò‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§ ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§¶‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§Æ‡•É‡§∑‡§ø‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§§ ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§ß‡§ø‡§ó‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ô‡•ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•à‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§â‡§™‡§¨‡•É‡§Ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••‚Äô

Lord Hari manifested Himself and told: ‚ÄúGreat gods! I am pleased (with your prayer). Indra, may welfare attend you all; go to that eminent sage Dadhichi and beg of him his body, strong with his Mantra, austerities and penances; tarry not. Sought by you, that sage who knows the Dharma will give his limbs (to you) andthen, there shall be an excellent weapon made out of those limbs by Visvakarman, by which, you shall, reinforced by my power, take off the head of Vritra."

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§ß‡•á ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡••

Having directed Indra thus, Hari disappeared at that very place.

‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§•‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§£‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‚Äò‡§ï‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Å ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

The great sage Dadhichi was accordingly besought by the gods (for his limbs): ‚ÄúO Brahmin! for men who are compassionate towards beings, what is there that is too hard to part with?‚Äù

** ‡§ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**

‚Äú‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§®‡§æ‡§•‡§æ ‡§® ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§Ø‡§∂‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§à‡§π‡•á‡§§ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§¶‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏ ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•à‡§∞‡§™‡§ø‡••‚Äù

The sage‚Äî

‚ÄúMasters! he is to be pitied even by inanimate things who, with kindness to beings, desires not (to secure) through his impermanent body Dharma or fame."

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ô‡§æ‡§•‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡§∞‡•á ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡§Ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§π‡•å‡••

Having determined thus, Dadhichi offered his soul to the Supreme Lord, the Brahman, and gave up his body.

‡§Ö‡§•‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ‡•§
‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§á‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Then, taking up the thunderbolt made by Visvakarman with the bones of sage Dadhichi, elated Indra, backed up by the power of the Lord, attacked Vritra for cutting him (to pieces), like angry Rudra attacking the god of death himself.

‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•à‡§∞‡§£‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§É‡••

Then there was a very terrific battle between the gods and the demons.

‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ò‡§æ‡§É
‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ó‡§£‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø
‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§É‡••

All the efforts the demons made against the gods were repeatedly rendered futile. Deprived of their strength, they made up their minds to forsake their master (Vritra) at the war-front, and flee.

‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑ ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡•§

‚Äò‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§É
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§® ‡§ö‡•á‡§π ‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡•É‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡•§
‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§∂‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§• ‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§Ç
‡§ï‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§µ‡•É‡§£‡•Ä‡§§ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

The firm-minded Vritra, seeing those Asura-followers of his fleeing, said this: “Death is certain for everybody that is born, this death for which there is no remedy here. If through that death, there is going to be the heaven of the heroes and renown, who will not welcome it when it comes?

‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§§‡•ã ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ö‡§É ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§∏‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§®‡•ç ‡§≠‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§™‡§∞‡§æ [‡§®‡•É‡§™]‡••

Having lost their senses and intent on running away, the panic-stricken demons heeded not the words of their master who was thus speaking what was righteous.

‡§∏ ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•É‡§ß‡•á
‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§π‡§£‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§®‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§π‡§É
‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡•á‡§® ‡§π‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡••

Highly infuriated in that battle, the enemy of Indra (Vritra) beheld (Indra) the murderer of his own brother armed with the thunderbolt, and remembering that sinful and wicked act of his, became sorrowful and clouded in mind, and spoke laughing (derisively):

‚Äò‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§É
‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡§æ ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§π‡§æ ‡§ö‡•§
‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§®‡•É‡§£‡§æ‡•á‡§Ω‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡§Æ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ
‡§Æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•É‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúLuckily you are standing before me as my enemy, you who are the murderer of a Brahmin, the murderer of a preceptor, the murderer of a brother! Luckily, O, you evil Indra, I shall now requite quickly by shattering your stone-heart with my trident.

‚Äò‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•á‡§∂ ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡•ã‡§∑‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç
‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§É‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡•á‡§ò‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§® ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑ ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§µ ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ
‡§π‡§∞‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§ß‡•Ä‡§ö‡•á‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§

‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§π‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Å‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ã
‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§É‡••

‚ÄúKing of the gods, why do you not aim your unfailing thunderbolt at me, your enemy standing in front of you? Indra, this thunderbolt is sharp not with your power, it is sharp by the power of God Hari and the penance of (sage) Dadhichi. Directed by Lord Vishnu, kill your enemy with that weapon itself. Where Lord Hari is, there victory, prosperity and all excellences are.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§π‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§π
‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§∞‡§Ç‡§π‡•ã‡§≤‡•Å‡§≤‡§ø‡§§‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡•ã
‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§É‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúAs God said, I shall concentrate my mind on His lotus-feet and with my ties of attachment to low things cut by the force of your thunderbolt, and casting off this body, I shall reach the sages goal.‚Äù

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§É [‡§®‡•É‡§™] ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ú‡•å
‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§∂‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç
‡§π‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ ‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡••

Desiring thus to lay down his body in the battle, considering as he did death better than victory, Vritra ran at Indra, grasping his trident, and spoke in anger: ‚ÄúSinner! you are killed.”

‡§π‡§®‡•å ‡§§‡§§‡§æ‡§°‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§•‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•á‡§≠‡§Ç
‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ò‡•ã‡§®‡§É‡••

Vritra then struck Indra, the chief of the gods, on the chin; and the thunderbolt fell from the hand of Indra.

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§-
‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡•å ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‚Äò‡§π‡§∞ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã
‡§ú‡§π‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§¶‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§É‚Äô‡••

Ashamed, Indra did not take up, in the presence of his enemy, the thunderbolt that had slipped down from his hand. Vritra told him: ‚ÄúIndra, take the thunderbolt and kill your enemy; this is no time for sorrow.‚Äù

‚Äò‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∂‡§æ ‡§µ‡§∂‡•á‡•§
‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§∂‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§á‡§π ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ì‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡•ã ‡§¨‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§ö‡•§
‡§§‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§®‡•ã ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§ú‡§°‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§

‚ÄúTime is the cause (of everything) here, Time under whose control, these worlds with their guardians live helplessly, like birds caught in a net. Not understanding that Time is energy, power, strength, life, immortality and death, man regards his foolish self as the cause.

‚Äò‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§§‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§®‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É‡••

‚ÄúGod creates beings with beings and Himself destroys beings with beings. Life, fortune, fame, lordship and all the blessings of man appear in the time propitious for them, even as their opposites appear (at other times) though man does not wish for them.

‚Äò‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ø‡§∂‡§∏‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§ú‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡§™‡§ø‡•§
‡§∏‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúTherefore one should be equanimous in infamy and fame, defeat and victory, miscry and happiness, and death and life.‚Äù

** ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã ‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§µ ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ä‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•Ä‡•§
‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§É‡••‚Äô

** Indra‚Äî**

‚ÄúHail, you demon! you have attained salvation, you whose mind has become thus; for you have cast away your demoniac nature and become a great man.‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ç‡§™‡§§‡•Ä‡••

Thus speaking to each other, the two chiefs of the warriors fought.

‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§π‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§≠‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§≤‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§â‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§ ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§∂‡•É‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ‡•å‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ‡••

Vritra got at Indra and swallowed him along with his elephant. The powerful Indra tore his stomach with his thunderbolt, and getting out, forcefully chopped off his head, like the summit of a mountain.

‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§É [‡§Ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ]‡•§
‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡••

Even as all the worlds were looking on, the effulgence of the Spirit that emanated from out of Vritra’s body attained the Lord who is beyond all worlds.

‡§Ö‡§•‡•á‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ß‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§ö‡§Ø‡•ã [‡§®‡•É‡§™]‡•§
‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§∂‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§®‡•Ä‡§π‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§®‡§æ‡••

Then, when the Supreme Being, the embodiment of all gods, was worshipped with sacrifice, that accumulation of sin due to the killing of the (Brahmin) sons of Tvashta, though very great, was completely removed by the Lord Himself, as mist is by the sun.

‡••‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§µ‡§ß‡§ï‡§•‡§æ‡••

_____

THUS ENDS THE STORY OF THE
KILLING OF VRITRA ASURA

‡••‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É‡••

‡••‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

_______

THE STORY OF PRAHLADA

_______

‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§® ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡§® ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§™‡•Ç‡§§‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§®‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

It is my decided opinion that man cannot become so much absorbed in God even through devotion, as he can through persistent enmity. Purified of their sins by their enmity, (the enemies of God) have attained Him through their continuous thought of Him.

‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¢‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•á ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§¶‡§ò‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¨‡§π‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ã ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§É‡••

As in devotion, so also in love, hate, fear and friendship, many have concentrated their minds on God, cast off their sin and attained to His goal,‚Äîthe shepherd-women in love, Kamsa in fear, and kings like Sisupala in hate.

‡§è‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Å‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§∏‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§É‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•å ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∑‡•á‡§ß‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Once, Sanandana and others, the sons of Brahma, went by chance to the world
of Vishnu; the two door-keepers (there) prevented them (from entering).

‡§Ö‡§∂‡§™‡§®‡•ç ‚Äò‡§Ü‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§∂‡•å ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§É‡••

The sages cursed (the two door-keepers): ‚ÄúChildish (Jaya and Vijaya)! away from here and quickly take demoniac births.‚Äù

‡§ú‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡•å‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•å ‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•å‡•§
‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∂‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡§æ‡•á ‡§π‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ã‡§ß‡§∞‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§¨‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡•å‡§ï‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§™‡•Å‡§É‡••

The two door-keepers of Vishnu were born as the two sons of Diti, respected by all the demons, Hiranyakasipu the elder,

and Hiranyaksha, the younger. Hiranyaksha was killed by the Lord who took the form of the Boar, when He lifted the earth out of the waters.5

‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§æ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§°‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡•§
‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∂‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§É [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ö‡§æ‡••

When his brother had been killed thus by Hari in the form of the Boar, Hiranyakasipu burnt with anger and grief.

‡§ï‡•ã‡§™‡•ã‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡§Æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‚Äò‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ ‡§ó‡§æ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§Ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡§™‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§ ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Ä‡§™‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§µ‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§§‡••‚Äô

With eyes blazing with anger, he told this to the demons: ‚ÄúWherever there are Brahmins, cows, Vedas, the preservation of Varna and Asrama and the practice of the duties of these, proceed to those places, and burn and slaughter.‚Äù

‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∂‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§É [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§Ö‡§ú‡•á‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ú‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§§‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§§‡•á‡§™‡•á ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§™‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

And Hiranyakasipu desired to make himself an invincible person, free from old age and death, and the sole monarch without a foe. (To this end) he performed very terrible penance in a ravine of the Mandara mountain.

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§ú‡§ú‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ã ‡§¶‡§∂‡••

When he was performing penance, all the ten quarters were ablaze.

‡§§‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡§æ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡§Ç‡§∏‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§®‡§É‡•§
‚Äò‡§µ‡§∞‡§¶‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‚Äô‡••

Brahma told that Hiranyakasipu who was burning the worlds with (the fire) of his penance : ‚ÄúI have come (here), the bestower of boons; choose your desired boon.‚Äù

‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∂‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã‡•§
‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§® ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•å ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§∞‡•á ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§® ‡§®‡§∞‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§® ‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡•à‡§∞‡§™‡§ø‡•§
‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§Æ‡§π‡•ã‡§∞‡§ó‡•à‡§É‡••

Hiranyakasipu :

“Lord! let me not have death from any of the beings created by you; let me not have death indoors or outside, by day or night, or from any other thing, or by any weapons; let me not have death on the ground or in the air, by men or by animals, by animate or inanimate things, or from gods, demons or the great serpents.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß ‡§ê‡§ï‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡••‚Äô

“(Also bestow on me) the state of being without an opponent in battle, the sole sovereignty over men and the power of all the gods, a power like that you possess.

‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡§§‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≤‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡••

Asked for boons (in that manner), Brahma gave him those boons hard to be obtained.

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§¨‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§™‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡••

Having thus obtained the boons, the demon, endowed with a golden body, began to hate the Lord, constantly remembering the killing of his brother.

‡§∏ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡§π ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ‡••

Conquering all the quarters and the three worlds, the great demon deprived the gods of their places and power.

‡§Æ‡§π‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§¶‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ñ‡§ø‡§≤‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

He occupied the very abode of Indra, possessed of every kind of prosperity.

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§ï‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§∂‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Frightened at his tyranny, all the worlds with their guardians (the gods), failing to get refuge elsewhere, went to the imperishable Lord Hari, for refuge.

‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§≠‡•Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡•Ä ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ò‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡•§
‚Äò‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§≠‡•à‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•å‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§∂‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡••

An incorporeal voice like the rumbling of the clouds manifested itself to them: ‚ÄúGreat gods! fear not; let there be

welfare to you all. I have known the wickedness of this Hiranyakasipu. the worst of demons. I will put an end to him, but wait for a time.

‚Äò‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ó‡•ã‡§∑‡•Å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§∑‡•Å‡•§
‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•Å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••

‚ÄúWhen one hates gods, Vedas, cows, Brahmins, good men, Dharma and Myself,
he perishes soon.‚Äù

‚Äò‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•á‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúWhen however he turns inimical towards his own son Prahlada, a great soul, devoid of any feeling of enmity and completely tranquil, I will kill him, though he is strong with boons.‚Äù

‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•å‡§ï‡§∏‡•ã ‡§ó‡§§‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§ó‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•á ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§π‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The gods became rid of their mental distress and took the demon as killed.

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§∏‡§ï‡§É‡••

The demon-king, Hiranyakasipu, had four marvellous sons; by (his) virtues, Prahlada, a worshipper of the great, was the greatest of them.

‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§≤‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã ‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§É‡•§
‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ô‡§ø‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§É‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§≤‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¢‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

Prahlada wasbeneficent to Brahmins, endowed with character, vowed to truthfulness, and one who had conquered his senses; like the soul, he was the one most beloved friend of all beings; at the feet of the noble, he was prostrate like a servant; and towards the suffering, he was affectionate like a father; he was attached like a brother towards his equals and had the regard of God for his elders; (though) endowed with birth, beauty, wealth and learning, he was devoid of the stiffness of pride.

‡§®‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§®‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§π‡§É
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§¶‡•É‡§ï‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡•á‡§∞‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§É‡••

His mind was unalarmed in calamities; he had no craving for the pleasures of this world or of the other heard of in sacrificial scripture, having found them unreal; with senses, breath, body and mind always under control, and with Desire completely extinct, Prahlada, though a demon by birth, was free from the demoniac nature.

‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•à‡§∞‡§≤‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ø‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡•à‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

Enough with innumerable virtues; sufficiently indicated is the greatness of one who delights in Lord Vasudeva by his very nature.

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡•§
‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∂‡§ø‡§™‡•Ç [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§Ö‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡••

Against that great devotee of the Lord, the blessed and great Prahlada, his own son, Hiranyakasipu sinned (by hating him).

‡§è‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§∞‡§æ‡§ü‡•ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø [‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ]‡•§
‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ ‡§ï‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡••

Once, the demon-king took his son (Prahlada) on his lap, and asked him: ‚ÄúTell me, child, that which you consider good.‚Äù

** ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§É‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç
‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§ï‡•Ç‡§™‡§Ç
‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡••‚Äô

** Prahlada‚Äî**

‚ÄúO eminent demon! That I consider good for men who are ever alarmed in mind in their false notion of I and Mine, namely, that man should abandon the house, the well hidden for his fall, and having gone to the forests, should seek Hari.‚Äù

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§∏ ‚Äò‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡§∞‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡••

‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡•ã ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ó‡•á‡§π‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Å‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§® ‡§≠‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‚Äô‡••

Having heard his son’s words in praise of his enemy, the demon laughed: ‚ÄúThe minds of boys are liable to be changed by those of others. Let the boy be well watched over by Brahmins in our preceptor’s residence so that his mind is not changed by the adherents of Vishnu, who move concealed.‚Äù

‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡§ï‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡••

The priests of the demon called forth Prahlada, who had been brought to their
residence, extolled him in fine words and asked of him in conciliatory terms:

‚Äò‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•É‡§∑‡§æ‡•§
‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§∑ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§≠‡•á‡§¶‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§ ‡§â‡§§‡§æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡•á‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡••‚Äô

“Dear Prahlada, welfare unto you; speak truth and not falsehood: Wherefore

is this affection of your mind which is beyond the range of boys? Is this the work of another or do you have it yoursel?‚Äù

** ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§É‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§É‡§™‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§É
‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§É ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§®‡§Æ‡§É‡••
‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äå ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡•å
‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≠‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§ö‡•à‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§Ø‡§æ‡••‚Äô

** Prahlada‚Äî**

‚ÄúObeisance unto that Lord whose Maya it is that causes in men the false notion of ‚Äòone‚Äôs own‚Äô and ‚Äòanother‚Äô, a notion seen (only) in those of deluded minds. As a piece of iron, O Brahmin, moves of itself in the presence of a magnet, even so is my mind affected unaccountably by Lord Hari‚Äôs presence.‚Äù

‡§§‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§• ‡§ï‡•Å‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‚Äå‡••

Then, that wretched servant of the king (the Brahmin teacher) became angry, and threatening Prahlada, made him receive his teaching of Dharma, Artha and Kama.

‡§§‡§§ ‡§è‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§Ø‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π [‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞]‡••

Finding then that Prahlada had learnt the four subjects (of the kings,-conciliation, bribing, creating dissensions and punishment by war), the preceptor showed him to the demon-king. The demon hailed him with blessings, and embracing him with his arms for long, he said this:

‚Äò‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•Ç‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§§ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúPrahlada, my child! recite something which you have learnt well, that which is best.”

** ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§É‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•å ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§æ‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ω‡§ß‡•Ä‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

Prahlada‚Äî

‚ÄúListening to and Singing of the glories of Vishnu, Thinking of Him, Service at His feet, Worshipping Him. Bowing to Him, Becoming a servant of His, Having a friend’s love for Him, Offering up of oneself to Him,‚Äîif man practises this ninefold devotion to Lord Vishnu, well, that I consider as the greatest learning.‚Äù

‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§µ‡§ö‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∂‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡•§
‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§´‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§ß‡§∞‡§É‡••

Hearing then these words of his son, Hiranyakasipu, with his lip quivering in fury, spoke this to the son of the preceptor:

‚Äò‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡§§‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•á‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúYou wretched Brahmin of evil mind! What is this? Ignoring me, you have vilely sided with the enemy and have taught this boy worthless things!‚Äù

‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§® ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡•Ä‡§§‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§™‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡•Ä‡§§‡§Ç
‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡•ã‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑ ‡§§‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡•§
‡§®‡•à‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç
‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§¶‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§®‡§É‡••‚Äô

The teacher’s son‚Äî

‚ÄúEnemy of Indra! this that your son speaks, was taught neither by me nor by anybody else. King! this state of mindhathcome to him by nature.Restrainyour ire and do not find fault with us.‚Äù

‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∂‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§® ‡§ö‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡§§‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§‚Äô

(Hiranyakasipu asked his son:) ‚ÄúIf this your eviland unfortunate attitude of mind is not learnt from your preceptor, wherefrom did you learn it?”

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§® ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•á ‡§™‡§∞‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ
‡§Æ‡§ø‡§•‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§ ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ó‡•ã‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç
‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

Prahlada‚Äî

‚ÄúFor those who are vowed to household life, and with unsubdued senses chew again and again the same cud and (thus) plunge into darkness, the thought of Krishna will be neither from another, nor of themselves, nor mutually.‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§∞‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∂‡§ø‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ä‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§≤‡•á‡••

In his rage, the blinded Hiranyakasipu flung on the ground from his lap his son who had spoken thus andfinished.

‡§Ü‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§É ‡§ï‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Ä‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§®‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§ã‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡••
‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§π‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ß‡§Æ‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§µ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§§‡§ø‚Äô‡••

Possessed by intolerant anger and with eyes turned red, Hiranyakasipu said: ‚ÄúLet this Prahlada be put to death, this Prahlada

who deserves to be killed; demons! take him away. This Vishnu is the person who killed my brother and this base Prahlada, leaving his own friends, does servile worship at the feet of him who killed his own uncle.‚Äù

‡§®‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§ã‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ ‡§≠‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§∂‡•Ç‡§≤‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¶‡§Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§∞‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§õ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§∏‡•Ä‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡§®‡§û‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ç‡§≤‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•Å‡••

Those demons ordered by their Lord, armed with tridents, their faces terrible with sharp fangs and shouting ‚Äòcut him, tear him‚Äô, struck with their tridents Prahlada who was sitting, at all the vital parts of his body.

‡§™‡§∞‡•á ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ñ‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡•§
‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§´‡§≤‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§∏‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∂‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§® [‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞]‡••

(Those tortures) were futile against Prahlada who had riveted his soul on the supreme Brahman, the inscrutable Lord, the soul of all. Fearing (the impossibility of killing him), the lord of the demons sough pertinaciously (several) means of killing him.

‡§¶‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§ó‡§ú‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∂‡•Ç‡§ï‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§®‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ó‡§∞‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•à‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§π‡§ø‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡§≤‡§ø‡§≤‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§£‡•à‡§∞‡§™‡§ø‡•§
‡§® ‡§∂‡§∂‡§æ‡§ï ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§Æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ò‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡••

With the elephants at the quarters, with serpents, by evil incantations, by throwing him down from heights, by black-magic, burials, poisonings, repeated starving, with cold, storm, fire, water, by rolling boulders on him,‚Äîwhen by all these means the demon could not kill his sinless son, he sank into deep thought but did not find a way of killing him.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Æ‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡•Ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡••‚Äô

(He said to himself:) ‚ÄúThis Prahlada is of inscrutable power; he has fear from nothing; he is indeed immortal; surely by (this) enmity (of mine) with him, there is going to be death for me, a thing new to me.‚Äù

‡§µ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§∞‡•Å‡§™‡§π‡•Ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§• ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡••

Then, when friends (in his class) called him, the great man of wisdom, Prahlada,
told them:

‚Äò‡§ï‡•å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§Ü‡§ö‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡•§
‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≤‡§≠‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§§‡§¶‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúA wise man should practise here virtues of devotion for the Lord in boyhood (itself), for this birth as man which has to give us our salvation is hard to be attained and, when attained, is impermanent.

‚Äò‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§π ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡§¶‡•á‡§∑ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúResorting to the feet of Lord Vishnu is proper for man here; for He is the beloved of all beings, the Soul, the Master and the Friend.

‚Äò‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Æ‡•à‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡§® ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§≤‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ã ‡§® ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§Ü‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúDemons! as misery comes to men without their effort for it, so also the pleasure of the senses is available for all beings by destiny and by the mere reason of their having taken a body. (Therefore) one should not strain oneself for its sake; for, by doing so, only life ebbs away.

‚Äò‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ã ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§∂‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ó‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ï‡•å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∂‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§ú‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∂‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡•á‡§® ‡§ö ‡§¨‡§≤‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ‡•§
‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡§ø‡••

‚ÄúA hundred years form a man’s life; the man who has no self-possession has but
half of that. Twenty years pass away for the fool in his sports of childhood and boyhood and a score (more) pass away as he remains inefficient for any work, his
body being in the grip of old age. The rest (also) passes away for the careless man who is engrossed is indomestic life in his insatiable desiresand strong infatuations.

‚Äò‡§ï‡•ã‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§§‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡•á‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§Ø ‡§à‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡•ã‡§µ‡§£‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúWho will renounce his desire for wealth, wealth which one desires to possess more than life, wealth which the thief, the servant and the merchant buy with their dear life?

‚Äò‡§î‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡•à‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É
‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ
‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É‡••

‚ÄúHow shall be become detached, he who esteems (only) the pleasures of sex and the palate and is in an endless delusion? Suffering with the threefold miseries¬πall around, he who delights in his family never gets disgusted (with his life).

‚Äò‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É
‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å‡•§
‡§â‡§™‡•á‡§§ ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç
‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•à‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§É‡••

________________________________________________________________

  1. Mental ills (Adhyatmika), physical ills (Adhibhautika) and calamities caused by forces of Nature, Fate and the gods (Adhidaivika).

________________________________________________________________

‚ÄúTherefore, ye demons! discard from a distance association with the demons of material pleasure. Go unto Narayana, the Prime Lord. He is the salvation desired by those who have given up all attachments.

‚Äò‡§® ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§π‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§É‡••
