THE STORY OF THE INCARNATION AS THE FISH

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734341617Screenshot2024-11-28134235.png"/>

‡§ó‡•ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§π‡§ø‡••

Desiring to protect Cows, Brahmins, gods, good men, the Vedas, Dharma, and Artha also, the Lord assumes bodily forms.

‡§Ü‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§®‡•à‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§≤‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã [‡§®‡•É‡§™]‡••

At the end of the last aeon, there was an involution caused by Brahma going to sleep. In that involution, the Earth and other worlds became deluged by the oceans.

‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§∂‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∑‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§≤‡•Ä‡•§
‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§µ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§Ω‡§π‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡••

The powerful Hayagriva (a demon), who was near, carried away the Vedas that had emanated from the face of the creator who desired to close his eyes in the sleep that came upon him on account of the aeon-end.

‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§∂‡§´‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‡••

Learning of that act of the demon-chief Hayagriva, Lord Hari assumed the form of a Fish.

‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§É ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§™‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§≤‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ‡§∂‡§®‡§É‡••

At that time, a great royal sage, Satyavrata by name, was performing penance, absolutely devoted to Narayana, sustaining himself on water alone.

‡§è‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§§‡•ã ‡§ú‡§≤‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡§ï‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§´‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ω‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡••

Once, as he was offering water-libation in the Kritamala river, there came a tiny fish with the water into his hard.

‡§ï‡§≤‡§∂‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å ‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≤‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§æ ‡§§‡•Å ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§ï‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§≤‡•å‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§è‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§ ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§¶‡•å‡§¶‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡•ã‡§¶‡§ï‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§§‡•§
‡§§‡§§ ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ã‡§µ‡§∞‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§§‡•§
‡§ú‡§≤‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ø‡•á ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡§ú‡•ç‡§ù‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The compassionate Satyavrata placed it in the water in his pitcher and took it to his hermitage. In a night, it grew in size in that pitcher. Satyavrata took it out of the pitcher and placed it in the water in atub. Placed there, it grew to three arms’ length in a moment. It was taken out of it and thrown into a big lake by the king. That great fish pervaded the lake with its body and was (still) growing continuously. The king (then) threw into the ocean that fish which was filling every kind of reservoir of water.

‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á‡§£ ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡••

Satyavrata asked it: “Who are you that bewilder us in the form of a fish?”

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî

‘‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ω‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡§∞‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡•ã‡§ß‡•å ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§

The Lord‚Äî

" O, subduer of enemies! on the seventh day from to-day, these three worlds, the Bhu, the Bhuva and others, shall become submerged in the ocean of the deluge.

‘‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§≠‡§∏‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡•§
‡§â‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡•å‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡••

“When, at that time, all the three worlds disappear in the waters of that dissolution, a spacious boat sent by me shall approach you.

‘‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•ã‡§∑‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¨‡•Ä‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§µ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡•§
‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§¨‡•É‡§Ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡•É‡§π‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡§¨‡§É‡••

“And, taking with you every kind of herb and every kind of sced, surrounded by the seven sages and every kind of animal, you shall get into that big ark and move about without any fear.

‘‡§¶‡•ã‡§ß‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§¨‡§≤‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ‡•§
‡§â‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∂‡•É‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§¨‡§ß‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§π‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡••

“Fasten with a long snake to the snout of Myself, who would approach you (at the proper time), that ark which would be tossed about by a forceful gale.

‘‡§Ö‡§π‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§∑‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã‡••

‡§Æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§ø‡••’

“King! I shall drag you along with the sages and the boat in the ocean and move about till Brahma’s night comes. to an end. And you shall also realise in your owe heart My glory, that which is called the Supreme Spirit, which I shall bless you with and expound in reply to your questions.”

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ß‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•§
‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡•à‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§ ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§ø‡§£‡§É‡••

Having directed the king thus, Lord Hari vanished. The king awaited that time, contemplating the Lord in the guise of the Fish.

‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§≤‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ò‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡••

Then the ocean was seen to rise as a result of huge clouds pouring down, and over-flow the coast and flood the earth all around.

‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§¶‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•á ‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã‡§π ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø‡•å‡§∑‡§ß‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•Å‡§ß‡§É‡••

While he was contemplating the command of the Lord, Satyavrata beheld the boat approach. Taking the medicinal herbs and other creepers, he got into it along with the best Brahmins.

‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§µ‡•á‡•§
‡§è‡§ï‡§∂‡•É‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ß‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π‡•à‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡§É‡••

Thought of by the king, the Lord ‘hen appeared in the great ocean, a golden Fish with a single snout, (full) nine million miles in length.

‡§®‡§ø‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•É‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§∏‡•Ç‡§¶‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç‡§≠‡•ã‡§ß‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§∞‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§∏‡§Ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ó‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§§‡§É‡••

Tying the ark to His snout, Satyvrata extolled the Lord. Sporting in the great ocean, the Lord in the form of the Fish imparted (to Satyavrata) the Truth as also the divine (Matsya) Purana and everything about the secret knowledge of the soul.

‡§Ö‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≤‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•á‡§ß‡§∏‡•á‡•§
‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§π‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡••

When the time of deluge-destruction had passed, Lord Hari killed the demon Hayagriva and restored the Vedas to Brahma, who had risen from his slumber.

‡§∏ ‡§§‡•Å ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§É‡••

By the grace of Lord Vishnu, that king Satyavrata, possessed of knowledge spiritual wisdom, became, Manu, the son of Vivasvan, in this (the next) aeon.

‡••‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§•‡§æ‡••

____________

THUS ENDS THE STORY OF THE INCARNATION AS THE FISH.

‡••‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É‡••

THE STORY OF THE INCARNATION AS RAMA

_________

‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§¶‡§∂‡§∞‡§•‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§Ç‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•á‡§® ‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£ ‡§≠‡§∞‡§§ ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§ò‡•ç‡§®‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

There was the emperor Dasaratha to whom Lord Hari, the Supreme Being, requested by the gods, partially manifested Himself as four sons, with the names Rama, Lakshmana, Bharata and Satrughna.

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∞‡§ø [‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ] ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Å‡§É‡•§

The story of that Lord Hari (as Rama), the husband of Sita, has been extensively described by sages who have realised the Truth, and has been frequently heard.¬π

‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§∞‡§¶‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç
‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É
‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•É‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§™‡§•‡§∞‡•Å‡§ú‡•ã
** ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π‡§∞‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§**
‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§£‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§π‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ
** ‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•É‡§Ç‡§≠‚Äî**
‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡•á‡§§‡•Å‡§É ‡§ñ‡§≤‡§¶‡§µ‡§¶‡§π‡§®‡§É
** ‡§ï‡•ã‡§∏‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§É‡••**

May that Rama protect us, Rama who abandoned the kingdom for the sake of his father and wandered from forest to forest with His lotus‚Äîfeet that could hardly bear even the touch of His beloved’s hand,

___________________________________________________________________________

1.THE RAMAYANA. Condensed in the poet’s own words and translated into English. Re. 1-4. G. A. Natesan & Co.

whose fatigue from walking was removed by Hanuman, the greatest of the monkeys and His own brother (Lakshmana), who in his fury at His separation from His beloved which resulted from His causing Surpanakha (the demoness) to be disfigured, frightened the ocean with the knit of His brow, built the dam, burnt the forest of the wicked (the demons) and became the king of the Kosalas.

‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§Ç
‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ú‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á ‡§∏‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Ø‡§ø‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç
‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§µ‡§®‡§Æ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§®‡§ø‡§µ ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§É‡••

Rama, who, with His wife, received with reverence the command of His father, who was tied by the chords of Truth, even though the father was a slave to a woman, and went away to the forest leaving His kingdom, riches, dear friends and His abode, even as as a person of detachment would give up his life.

‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ã‡§ß‡§Æ‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡•É‡§ï‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§®‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç
‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§¶‡•Å‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§µ‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§£‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É
‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡••

Who, when (his beloved), the daughter of the king of the Videhas, was carried away in His absence in the forest by the base demon (Ravana) as by a wolf, and became separated from from His beloved, wandered about in the forest along with His brother (Lakshmana) like some pitiable person, thereby making clear the fate of those attached to women.

‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡§ø ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡•á‡•§
‡§®‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ú‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡§≠‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‘‡§è‡§ï‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ß‡§∞‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§ß‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡••

When the righteous Rama who brought happiness to all beings was king, there did not exist mental and physical maladies, old-age, fatigue, misery, sorrow, fear and

weariness. Upholding the vow of devotion to one wife, living the life of a royal sage, and remaining pure, Rama Himself observed His His Dharma as a householder, (thereby) teaching it (to the world).

‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ï‡§ï‡§£‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§™‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§É‡••

Imprinting in the hearts of those who remembered Him, His sprout‚Äîlike feet, pricked by the thorns of the Dandaka forests, Rama went away from Ayodhya to His own effulgent abode.

‡§®‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ã ‡§∞‡§ò‡•Å‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§§‚Äî
‡§≤‡•Ä‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡§®‡•ã‡§∞‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ß‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ã‡§µ‡§ß‡•ã ‡§ú‡§≤‡§ß‡§ø‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡•Ç‡§ó‡•à‡§É
‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡§®‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§™‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É‡••

This, the annihilation of the demons and the damming of the ocean with (the power of) His arrows, is hardly any glory for that king of the Raghus, who assumed in sport that form at the entreaty of the

gods, and whose greatness hath nothing either to excel or equal it. Are monkeys His aids in the killing of His foes?

‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§£‡•à‡§∞‡•Å‡§™‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§®‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§∞‡•ã [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••

The person who listens to and imbibes the story of Rama becomes devoted to the path of non-wickedness and gets liberated from the ties of Action.

THE STORY OF THE INCARNATION AS PARASURAMA

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734588700Screenshot2024-12-19114104.png"/>

‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§ú‡§Æ‡§¶‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§π ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§µ‡§ã‡§∑‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§É‡••

‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§π‡•à‡§π‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Ø ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§É‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Jamadagni married Renuka, the daughter of Renu. Of her and that sage of the Bhrigu line (Jamadagni), was born the very well known Rama, who, they say, was a partial incarnation of Lord Vasudeva, the annihilator of the race of the Haihayas, He who, twenty-one times, swept this earth clean of the Kshatriyas.

**‡§π‡•à‡§π‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡§É‡•§
‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∂‡§∂‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•á‡§≠‡•á ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å‡•• **

‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•à‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§®‡•ç ‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß ‡§∏‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Å‡§ú‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§¶‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•á‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§™‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡••

There was the greatest of the Kshatriyas, Arjuna (Kartavirya), the king of the Haihayas, who obtained a thousand arms and inviolability by foes. Sporting (in the waters) with his excellent women, he dammed the river with his arms: and the ten-headed Ravana, he imprisoned and released as one would a monkey.

‡§∏ ‡§è‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§™‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§Æ‡§¶‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§∞‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§®‡§∞‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§£‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§∏‡•à‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§π‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡§™‡•ã‡§ß‡§®‡§É‡••

Once he came into the hermitage of Jamadagni. The sage for whom penance was his wealth, offered hospitality to that king with all his army, ministers and animals, with the aid of his Kamadhenu.

‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§® ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§π‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•É‡§∑‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§® ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ö‡•ã‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡•á ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É ‡§∏‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

The valorous Arjuna saw in that hermitage of Jamadagni that excelling of his own wealth. In his pride, he set his men to carry away Kamadhenu ; and they forcibly took to Mahishmati (Arjuna’s capital) that bleating cow with its calf.

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§Ü‡§ó‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•å‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§ò‡•ã‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§∂‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§§‡•Ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡§§ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§•‡§™‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Then, when the king had gone, Rama, who had returned, heard in the hermitage of that wickedness of Arjuna and became furious like a beaten serpent. Seizing his terrible axe, quiver, shield and bow, the inviolable Rama ran after Arjuna, like a lion running after an elephant.

‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§®‡•ç
‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ã‡§¶‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§•‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•å‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡•Ä‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§∂‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∑‡§£‡§æ‡§É
‡§§‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§è‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•Ç‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡••

Arjuna beheld Him rushing, as he was entering his city, and directed (against Him) seventeen formidable Akshauhinis¬π of elephants, chariots, horses and foot. Singly, Lord Rama destroyed them.

‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§∂‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‚Äî
‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å ‡§¨‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ó‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ß‡•á‡•§
‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡•Ä‚Äî
‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§ï‡§ß‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§ø‡§®‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Then Arjuna simultaneously aimed at Rama arrows from the five‚Äîhundred bows in his arms. Rama, the foremost of the wielders of missiles, simultaneously cut all his bows with the arrows of but one bow.

__________________________________________________________________________

1.An Akshauhini is an unit of army comprising 21,870 elephants, 21,870 chariots, 65,610 horse and 109,350 foot.

‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•à‡§∞‡§ö‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É‡§ß‡•á‡§Ω‡§ô‡•ç‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•ç
‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡•á‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡•§
‡§≠‡•Å‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§†‡§æ‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§ï‡§†‡•ã‡§∞‡§®‡•á‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ
‡§ö‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§¶ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§≠‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡••

Of that Arjuna who, once again, lifted mountains and trees in his hands and rushed forward in battle, Rama, forcibly cut the arms and severed the head with his sharpedged battle‚Äîaxe.

‡§π‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§π‡§æ‡•§
‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏, ‡§ú‡§Æ‡§¶‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§§‡••

When their father was killed, Arjuna’s sons, numbering ten thousand, fled in fear. Rama, the destroyer of enemy‚Äîwarriors, recovered the cow along with her calf, reached the hermitage and gave the muchharassed cow to his father. Rama described his exploit, (whereon) Jamadagni (his father)said :

‘‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§∑‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∞‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•É‡§•‡§æ‡••

“Rama, mighty‚Äîarmed Rama ! you have committed a crime in that you in that you have, for no purpose, killed the king who is the embodiment of all gods.

‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§£‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∞‡•ã‡§ö‡§§‡•á ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•å‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•Å ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‡••

Son! we are Brahmins who become fit for honour because of our forbearance. It is by forbearance that Brahminic splendour shines like the light of the sun. sun. Hari, the Lord and Master, is quickly pleased with persons of forbearance.

‘‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ß‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§Ç‡§π‡•ã ‡§ú‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§®‡§É‡••’

“The murder of an anointed king is more heinous than the slaying of a Brahmin. And this sin, you wipe out by visiting the holy places, with your thought on the imperishable Lord.”

‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡§∂‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡•á‡§§‡§ø [ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§® ]‡•§
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§§‡•ç‡••

(Thus) instructed by His father, Rama made a pilgrimage to holy places for a year and returned to His hermitage.

‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§æ [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ] ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§è‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§ø ‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§¨‡•à‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ø‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∑‡§µ‡•ã ‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§Ü‡§∏‡•Ä‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§£‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ω‡§§‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡§É‡••

Remembering the killing of their father, the sons of Arjuna, getting an opportunity when Rama, along with his brothers, had once gone away from the hermitage into the forests, came ( to the hermitage) desiring to wreak vengeance. They saw the sage (Jamadagni) in the fire‚Äîchamber, sitting in meditation. Though entreated by the pitiable mother of Rama, those extremely cruel and base Kshatriyas forcibly chopped and carried off Jamadagni’s head.

‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§§‡•Ä‡•§
‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•á ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§π‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The virtuous wife of Jamadagni, Renuka, cried aloud :“Rama, Rama.” Rama hurried to the hermitage and found his father Killed.

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§∂‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§¶‡§ß‡•á‡••

Seizing his hatchet, Rama made up his mind to annihilate the Kshatriyas.

‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ò‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏ ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡•Ä [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§®‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ò‡•ã‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Going to Mahishmati, whose prosperity had already been destroyed by those murderers of the Brahmin, Rama raised a great mountain in the centre of the city, with the heads of those (sons of Arjuna), and with their blood, He created a terrible river, striking terror in the enemies of the Brahmins.

‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§É ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§É‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•á ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§∂‡•ã‡§£‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡••

Ridding the earth of Kshatriyas for twenty-one times, the Lord created nine lakes of blood at Syamantapanchaka.

‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞ ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡•§
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ñ‡•à‡§É‡••

Taking the head of His father, He joined it with the trunk, in the sacrifice, and worshipped with sacrifices the Lord, the embodiment of all gods, His own Self.

‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§Æ‡§¶‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ã‡§∑‡•Ä‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§≤‡•á ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡•Ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

Obtaining his body in the form of effulgence, Jamadagni, who was honoured by Rama, became the seventh in the group of the (seven great) sages.¬π

‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§Æ‡§≤‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•å ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ß‡•Ä‡§É‡••

___________________________________________________________________________

1.The group of the seven great sages (Sapta Rishis) is the constellation of the Great Bear. The seven great sages are Kasyapa, Atri, Vasishtha, Visvamitra, Gautama, Bharadvaja and Jamadagni.

And the Lord, the lotus‚Äîeyed Rama who incarnated Himself as the son of Jamadagni, is present even now in the Mahendra hill having laid down the function of punishment and become completely tranquil in mind.

‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•á‡§π ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§¶‡§æ ‡§§‡•Å ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§∂ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡••

Whenever there is the decline of Dharma and the increase of Adharma in this world, Hari, the Lord and Master, incarnates Himself.

‡••‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§∂‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§•‡§æ‡••

THUS ENDS THE STORY OF THE INCARNATION AS PARASURAMA.
