‡§¶‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§ ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§ï‡§æ‡§É
‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á‡••

“By your birth, the Vraja flourishes ever more, and here, the Goddess of Fortune abides permanently. Beloved Lord! see, those who are your own, those whose life are searching for you in (all) is in you, directions.

‘‡§® ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç
‡§Ö‡§ñ‡§ø‡§≤‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¶‡•É‡§ï‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§ñ‡§®‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡•á
‡§∏‡§ñ ‡§â‡§¶‡•á‡§Ø‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡•á‡••

“Verily, you are not the son of a cowherd-woman; you are the onlooker who is the inner soul of all beings. Friend! requested by Brahma to protect the universe, you arose in the arose in the race of the Satvatas.

‡§§‡§µ ‡§ï‡§•‡§æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç
‡§ï‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∑‡§æ‡§™‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§£‡§Æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§§‡§Ç
‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø ‡§ó‡•É‡§£‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§É‡••’

‚ÄúThey are the bestowers of plenty on earth who sing your nectar-like story, the rejuvenator of scorched souls, praised by men of vision, the destroyer of sin, auspicious to the ears, extensive and beautiful.‚Äù

‚Äú‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≤‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ß‡§æ‡•§
‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§≠‡•Ç‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•å‡§∞‡§ø‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ú‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§∞‡§ß‡§∞‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§•‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§•‡§É‡••

Thus did the Gopis sing and prattle in manifold ways. To them, Krishna manifested Himself, with His lotus-face smiling, wearing yellow garments and garlands and looking more Love-like than Love himself.

‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§´‡•Å‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ã‡§Ω‡§¨‡§≤‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ó‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§É ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Seeing Him, their most beloved Lord, who had come, the women, with their eyes blooming in love, rose up all together, even as bodies arise on seeing life coming.

‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§≤‡§ø‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡§≠‡§§ ‡§ó‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ã‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•à‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡•à‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡••

Taking them, Lord Krishna entered the sands of the Yamuna and there began the sport of the Rasa‚Äìdance18,accompanied by those beautiful women who were devoted to Him and who, in joy, had entwined each other’s arms.

‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§∞‡•á‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§≤‡•Ä‡§≤‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

Multiplying Himself into as many as the women, the Lord delighted with them in sport, though He revelled only in Himself.

__________

**‡§Ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡§ß‡§É‚Äî**THE KILLING OF ARISHTA

‚Äî‚Äî:0:‚Äî‚Äî

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡•ã ‡§ó‡•ã‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡§≠‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§ï‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§ñ‡•Å‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Then to the Gokula came Arishta, a demon in the form of a bull, with a huge hump and body, making the earth, stamped by his hooves, quake.

‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∂‡•É‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§ó‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É‡••

The Gopis and Gopas were frightened on seeing that bull of sharp horns. Crying ’ Krishna, Krishna’, they all went to Krishna for refuge.

‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏ ‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡•É‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É
‡§™‡§¶‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§ò‡§æ‡§® ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡•§
‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ã‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡§• ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§Ç
‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡•à‡§É ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§°‡§ø‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§É‡••

Krishna caught by its horns the bull that was rushing up, overpowered it by his foot and killed it; it fell down, suffered extreme pain and then passed away to the abode of death. The gods showered flowers and lauded Hari.

_________

**‡§ß‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É‚Äî**PREPARATIONS FOR THE BOW‚ÄìFESTIVAL

___________

‡§Ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§§‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§ï‡§ö‡§æ‡§£‡•Ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§≤‡§§‡•ã‡§∂‡§≤‡§ï‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ú‡§∞‡§æ‡§ü‡•ç‡••

When the demon Arishta had been killed by Krishna of wondrous deeds, Kamsa, the Bhoja king, then called Mushtika, Chanura, Sala, Tosalaka and other ministers of his and his elephant‚Äîkeepers and told them‚Äî

‘‡§≠‡•ã ‡§≠‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§ö‡§æ‡§£‡•Ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§ï‡•å‡•§
‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§ï‡§¶‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§≠‡•á‡§É‡•§
‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•å ‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É ‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤ ‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

“Hear this, O heroic Chanura and Mushtika ! In Nanda’s Vraja live Rama and Krishna, the sons of Vasudeva ; from them has death been foretold for me.

‘‡§≠‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§π ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•å ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§≤‡•Ä‡§≤‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

“They must be killed by you when they are brought here, in the sport of wrestling.

‡§Æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§∞‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•å‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

“Let various kinds of stands be put up, surrounding the wrestling ring. Let men from the city and the country witness the free fight.

‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§µ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡•Ä‡§°‡•ã‡§ú‡§π‡§ø ‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•å‡••

“You my good elephant‚Äîkeeper! Let the elephant Kuvalayapida be kept at the door of the arena and kill with it those two enemies of mine.

‘‡§Ü‡§∞‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡••’

And on the fourteenth day of this fortnight, let the worship of the bow be begun in the prescribed manner.

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡§π‡•§
‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§ò‡§æ‡§®‡§ï‡§¶‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§≠‡•á‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§ß‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ñ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••’

Having thus commanded, Kamsa, who was versed in the science of politics, said to Akrura: “Go to Nanda’s Vraja; there the two sons of Vasudeva live. Bring them along with Nanda and other Gopas with their tributes, for seeing the festival of the bow and the splendour of the Yadava capital.”

‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ï‡•Ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂ ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§∏‡§É ‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Having ordered Akrura also in this manner, Kamsa sent awayhis ministers and entered his apartment.And Akrura also went to his abode.

____________

**‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‚Äî**THE ARRIVALOF AKRURA

_________

‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ó‡•ã‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡§•‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ú‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡•á‡•§
‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§ó‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç’‡••

Mounting the chariot, Akrura went to the Gokula of Nanda. With great devotion to the lotus-eyed Lord, he thought on the way: “What auspicious thing did I do that I am going to see Lord Hari to-day?”

‡§∞‡§•‡•á‡§® ‡§ó‡•ã‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂ ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•á ‡§ó‡•ã‡§¶‡•ã‡§π‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡•å‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡•å ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡•å ‡§ú‡§ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§§‡•Ç‡§ú‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•Ä‡••

Akrura reached the Gokula in his chariot and the sun also set. He saw at the milking yard in the VrajaKrishna and Balarama, of charming faces,the foremost of the beautiful, the cause and theLords ofthe universe.

‡§∞‡§•‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Æ‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§≤‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ï‡•Ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡§¨‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡§™‡§æ‡§§ ‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É‡••

Quickly jumping down from his chariot, Akrura, trembling with love, fell like a stick at the feet of Rama and Krishna.

‡§™‡•Å‡§≤‡§ï‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó ‡§î‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§£‡•ç‡§†‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§ï‡§§‡•ç [‡§®‡•É‡§™]‡•§

‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§•‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡•§
‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§≠‡•á‡§Ω‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§§‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§≤‡§É‡••

With hairs standing on end, and lost in love, Akrura could not announce himself. Understanding who he was, the Lord who is affectionate to those who bow to Him, became pleased, drew Akrura to Himself with his discus-marked hand and embraced him.

‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§ó‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•Ä ‡§Ö‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡•ã ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The high-minded Balarama also embraced Akrura who had bowed to him, and taking Akrura’s hand in his, brought him home, along with his brother Krishna.

‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡•ã‡§™‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•á ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã‡§∞‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§µ‡§É‡••

Sitting comfortably on the cot and highly honoured by Rama and Krishna, Akrura, questioned by the Lord (about the purpose of his visit), related everything.

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ö‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã ‡§¨‡§≤‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§π‡§æ‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§§‡•Å‡§É‡••

Hearing the words of Akrura, Krishna and Rama, the destroyers of enemy warriors, laughed and informed their father Nanda of the command of their king, (Kamsa).

‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‚Äò‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡•ã‡§∞‡§∏‡§É‡•§
‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§ï‡§ü‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡•§
‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤‚Äô‡••

And Nanda commanded the cowherds: ‚ÄúCollect all the products of of our dairy;

let presents be taken and carts bemade ready. We shall proceed to Mathura to-morrow and give our products to the king. We shall witness the great festival. It is said, people from the countryside will go there.‚Äù

‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§ò‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§µ‡§¶‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡••

The Lord reached the sin-destroying Yamuna. Akrura took leave of Rama and Krishna, and performed ablution in the prescribed manner.

‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏‡§≤‡§ø‡§≤‡•á ‡§ú‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§µ ‡§¶‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•á‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•å ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•å‡••

Repeating the eternal Veda, Akrura in mersed himself and (there) in the waters of the Yamuna, he saw the Rama and Krishna together.

‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§´‡§£‡§Æ‡•å‡§≤‡§ø‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§ò‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Ä‡§§‡§ï‡•å‡§∂‡•á‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Again, Akrura beheld there (Adisesha), crested with a thousand hoods. And on his lap, the Supreme Being, cloud-blue, wearing yellow silk, four-armed, serene and with eyes red like the lotus-petal.

‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•å‡§∑‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§≤‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§ü‡§É ‡§∂‡§®‡•à‡§É‡••

With supreme devotion and with palms joined in respect, Akrura softly extolled the Lord.

‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§µ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ú‡§≤‡•á ‡§µ‡§™‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã ‡§®‡§ü‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡••

Having shown His form in the waters to Akrura who was extolling Him, Lord Krishna withdrew it again, even as a dancer would his dance.

‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§Æ‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡•ç ‡§π‡•É‡§∑‡•Ä‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§É ‚Äò‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•ã‡§Ø‡•á ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡•á‚Äô‡••

And Akrura, seeing the Lord disappear, came to the chariot, wondering. The Lord

asked him: ‚ÄúWhat is the wonder on earth, in the skies or in the waters that has been seen by you? You look like one who has seen a wonder.‚Äù

** ‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡§É‚Äî**

‡§Ö‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§π ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ú‡§≤‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ω‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§É‡••

Akrura‚Äî

‚ÄúWhatever wonders there are on earth, in the skies or in the waters, all of them are in you, who is of the form of the universe. What is it that has not been seen by me, who has truly seen?‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ö‡•ã‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§•‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•á‡••

Having said thus, (Akrura) the son of Gandini, drove the chariot and brought Rama and Krishna to Mathura when the day was coming to a close.

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734514221Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png”/>

** ‡§Æ‡§•‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§É‚Äî**

THE ENTRY OF THE LORD INTO MATHURA

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734514404Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png”/>

‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•å‡§ï‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡§µ‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡••

Meantime, Nanda andother cowherds had reached in advance the garden at the city gate, and remained there, awaiting (Rama and Krishna).

‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‚Äò‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡§π‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ó‡•á‡§π‡§Æ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡§Ç‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‚Äô‡••

Joining them, the Lord, who is the Master of the universe, said to Akrura: ‚ÄúEnter you first the city with the chariot and go to your house. After killing the enemy of the Yadus, I will go to your house with my elder brother, and please my friends.‚Äù

‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§á‡§µ‡•§
‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§É ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å‡••

So told by the Lord, Akrura became somewhat dejected, entered the city, informed Kamsa of his having done his work, and went to his house.

‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡•á ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§É ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§•‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•à‡§É ‡§¶‡§ø‡§¶‡•É‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

Then, in the afternoon (of the following day), Lord Krishna, accompanied by Balarama and surrounded by the cowherds, entered Madhura desiring to see (the city).

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§∂‡§ø‡§ñ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§¢‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§´‡•Å‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ú‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§¶‡§æ ‡§¨‡§≤‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§µ‡•å‡••

Mounting the tops of the mansions, ladies with their lotus-faces abloom with delight, showered heaps of flowers flowers on Balarama and Krishna.

‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•å‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§ß‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã ‡§¶‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•á ‡§ß‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡•à‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

The imperishable Lord then enquired of the citizens the place where the bow was, and entering that place, beheld the bow, wonderful like the rainbow, with most costly trappings, guarded by numerous men and kept worshipped.

‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§®‡•É‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¨‡§≠‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡•ã‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§É‡•§
‡§ß‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§É ‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡•ã‡§¶‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

Though prevented by the men, the exceedingly powerful Krishna broke the bow. The noise of the bow that was being broken filled the skies, heaven and earth, and (all) the quarters; and on hearing it, became alarmed.

‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ö‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§µ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•å ‡§ß‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§® ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§ï‡§≤‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ú‡§ò‡•ç‡§®‡§§‡•Å‡§É‡••

The guardians of the bow, along with their followers, surrounded (Krishna and Rama), shouting: ‚ÄúCatch them.‚Äù Infuriated, (Krishna and Rama) took two broken pieces of the bow and killed them.

‡§¨‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡•á‡§∞‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•å ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡•á‡§Ø‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•å ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•å ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§ï‡§ü‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§ä‡§∑‡§§‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ö‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

Having killed the forces sent by Kamsa also, the two went out of that apartment (of the bow) and wandered about merrily. The sun (then) set, and Krishna and Rama, surrounded by the cowherds, went out of the city, to where their carts were. Knowing what Kamsa desired to do, the two spent the night happily.

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734516449Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png”/>

** ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§∏‡§µ‡§ß‡§É‚Äî**

THE KILLING OF KAMSA

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734516568Screenshot2024-12-15104407.png”/>

‡§ï‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•å‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ö‡•§
‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§£‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•á‡§≠‡•á ‡§® ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

And Kamsa saw evil omens heralding death, became afraid of it and, in his anxiety, had no sleep.

‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§ø [‡§ï‡•å‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø] ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ö‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

When the night had come to an end and there was dawn and and the sun had risen out of the waters, Kamsa directed the great carnival of wrestling to be conducted.

‡§Æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§≤‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡§§‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§ö‡•à‡§≤‡§§‡•ã‡§∞‡§£‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§™‡•å‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§¶‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡§Ç‡§∏‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§Æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡••

The stands were decorated with garlands, flags and buntings.Citizens, country-folk and kings tooktheir seats there. Surrounded by hisministers, Kamsa sat in the king’s stand.

‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ ‡§¶‡•É‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡§§‡•§
‡§ö‡§æ‡§£‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§ï‡§É ‡§ï‡•Ç‡§ü‡§É ‡§∂‡§≤‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§∂‡§≤ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§ö‡•§

The bedecked and haughty wrestlers, Chanura, Mushtika, Kuta, Sala and Tosala, sat (there) with their teachers.

‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡§æ ‡§è‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Ü‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡••

Nanda and othercowherds occupied one stand.

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§∂‡•å‡§ö‡•å [‡§™‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™]‡•§
‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§¶‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ò‡•ã‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡•á‡§Ø‡§§‡•Å‡§É‡••

Then, Krishna and Rama, who had finished their bath, heard the rumblings of the wrestlers‚Äô drums, and came to witness (the tournament).

‡§∞‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§µ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡•Ä‡§°‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ã‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Reaching the gate of the arena, Krishna saw stationed there the elephant Kuvalayapida, set on Him by its keeper.

‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§≤‡•á‡•§
‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•á‡§≠‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡§®‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡••

The Lord threw on the ground the elephant that rushed (at Him). Plucking out its tusk, Krishna struckdeadthe elephant and its keepers, with it.

‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ã ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•à‡§É ‡§ï‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§Ø‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§≤‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•å‡•§
‡§∞‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡•Ç [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§ó‡§ú‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡•å‡••

Surrounded by a few cowherds and armed with the excellent weapons of the elephant‚Äôs tusks, Balarama and Krishna entered the arena.

‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•å ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡•å ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•É‡§∂‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•á [ ‡§®‡•É‡§™]‡••

Seeing those two, the invincible Krishna and Rama, Kamsa shook terribly with fear.

‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•å ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§£‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‚Äò‡§π‡•á ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∏‡•Ç‡§®‡•ã ‡§π‡•á ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•å ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•å‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ï‡•Å‡§∂‡§≤‡•å ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§π‡•Ç‡§§‡•å ‡§¶‡§ø‡§¶‡•É‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡•§
‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•á‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§≤‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§π ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§ï‡§É‚Äô‡••

Accosting Krishna and Rama, Chanurasaid: ‚ÄúOh! Krishna! Oh! Rama! being known as esteemed amidst warriors and

experts in wrestling, you have been called (here) by the king who desires to see (you in action). Fight with me, Balarama fight with Krishna, and let Balarama Mushtika.‚Äù

‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§ö ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§ó‡•Ä‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

Intertwining their arms and and legs, the two pairs forcibly pulled down each other for victory.

‡§¨‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§£‡•Ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§∂‡•ã ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ã‡§•‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§§‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä‡§£‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Seizing Chanura by his arms, Krishna wheeled him round many times and forcibly dashed him on the ground when his life was almost gone.

‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§ï‡•ã ‡§¨‡§≤‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§§‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§π‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§É, ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§∏‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•Å‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§≤‡§ò‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡••

Struck by the palm of Balarama, Mushtika died. The remaining wrestlers

fled. The imperishable Lord, who was very angry with Kamsa, lightly leapt and mounted the high stand (of the king) quickly.

‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§® ‡§Ü‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•Ä‡••

Seeing Him, his death, enter (his enclosure), the firm-minded Kamsa jumped up from his seat and took his sword and shield.

‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ñ‡§°‡•ç‡§ó‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•Å
‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡§∞‡§ø ‡§§‡•Å‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§É
‡§™‡§™‡§æ‡§§ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É‡••

That Kamsa who was was swiftly moving, sword in hand, the Lord threw down on the field from the high gallery; and upon him, fell the Lord who is master of Himself and is the abode of the whole universe.

‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡§§ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•å
‡§π‡§æ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ω‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡••

When Kamsa had died, the Lord dragged and there him along the ground; and were tremendous shouts of ‚ÄòHah, Hah‚Äô at that time.

‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ö‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§• ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•å ‡§µ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•á ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É‡••

Freeing then their mother and father from imprisonment, Krishna and Rama bowed, touching their feet with their heads.

‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§ó‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•å‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•å ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•å ‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•á ‡§®‡§∂‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡•å‡••

Devaki and Vasudeva understood their sons who who were bowing to them as the Lords of the universe and, free from fear embraced them.

<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734518836Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png”/>

‡§â‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∑‡•á‡§ï‡§É

THE INSTALLATION OF
UGRASENA AS KING
<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1734518836Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡•å ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

After lovingly consoling his parents, Lord Krishna made his maternal grandfather, Ugrasena, the king of the Yadus.

‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡§ï‡§Ç‡§∏‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡•á‡§π‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡••

All his kith and kin, who had fled in all directions out of their fear of Kamsa, the Lord, who is the creator of the universe, pleased with gifts of wealth and settled in their own homes.

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞] ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§É‡••

‚Äò‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§ ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§§ ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Æ‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

Coming to Nanda then, Lord Krishna and Balarama embraced him and said thus: ‚ÄúFather ! go to the Vraja and we shall go there to see our kinsmen sorrowing in their love for us, after looking to the welfare of our friends (here).‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•å ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ã ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å‡••

Told thus, Nanda embraced Krishna and Rama and, along with the cowherds, left for the Vraja.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734518836Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

** ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§É‚Äî **

LIFE WITH THE TEACHER

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734518836Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

‡§§‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•å ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•å‡•§
‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•å‡••

Then, receiving the sacraments and attaining to the state the state of the twice-born, Rama and Krishna, who observed the vows well, received initiation into the meditation of the Gayatri from Garga, the preceptor of the Yadus.

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§µ‡•å ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•å ‡§ú‡§ó‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•å‡•§
‡§Ö‡§•‡•ã ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡•á ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡•Å‡§™‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Ä‡§™‡§®‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Rama and Krishna, the Lords of the universe, omniscient and the source of all lores, then desired to study under a preceptor and approached Sandipani of the line of Kasyapa, living in the city of Avanti.

‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§§‡•å ‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§§‡•Å‡§É [‡§®‡•É‡§™]‡••

They imbibed everything on everything on a single utterance by the preceptor.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734518836Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

** ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§É‚Äî **

MESSAGE TO THE GOKULA THROUGH UDDHAVA

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734518836Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§ ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡•ã ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§É‡••
‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§π‡§∞‡•ã ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡••

There was the minister Uddhava, the greatest of the wise and a friend of Krishna. To him, His dearest friend, Lord Hari, the destroyer of the suffering of His devotees, said :

‚Äò‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡•å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡•§
‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ö‡§Ø‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúOh good-natured Uddhava! go to the Vraja and convey our love to our parents (Nanda, Yasoda and Rohini) and, with my message, remove the suffering of the Gopis at My separation.‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§ ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡•ã [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ó‡•ã‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡••

Thus told, Uddhava went to the Gokula of Nanda. Nanda, who was pleased, embraced him and worshipped him, regarding him as Krishna Himself.

** ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§É‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã ‡§ó‡§æ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§¨‡•É‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ó‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§ï‡•Å‡§¶‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Nanda‚Äî

‚ÄúDoes Krishna remember us, the cows, the Vrindavana and the mountain (Govardhana)? Will He come (here) once to see His kinsmen?

‚Äò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§≤‡•Ä‡§≤‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§π‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§É ‡§∂‡§ø‡§•‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É‡••

‚ÄúFor us who are recapitulating the exploits of Krishna, His sportive side-long glances, His laughter and His speech, Oh, all activities become slackened.

‚Äò‡§∏‡§∞‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•à‡§≤‡§µ‡§®‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§™‡§¶‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúFor us who are seeing the places of His sports, the river, the mountain and the forest regions adorned with His footprints, our mind becomes filled with Him.‚Äù

** ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡§É‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ñ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•å ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§ø ‡§∏ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡•à‡§ß‡§∏‡§ø‡••

Uddhava‚Äî

‚ÄúBlessed (Nanda and Yasoda!) do not feel pained; you shall see Krishna by your side. Like fire within the wood, He is within the heart of (all) beings.

‚Äò‡§®‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§ß‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡••

‚ÄúTo Him who does not have the sense of ‚Äúmy‚Äù, there is none who is (specially) dear, and none who is (specially) inimical; to Him who is equanimous (towards all), there is none who is superior, inferior or not equal.

‚Äò‡§Ø‡•Å‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•á‡§µ ‡§®‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏ ‡§à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‡••

‚ÄúThis Lord Hari is not the son the son of you two only; He is the Son, Soul, Father, Mother and Master of all.‚Äù

** ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§≠‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§π ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§ó‡•ã‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•á ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡•á‡••‚Äô

** The Gopis told Uddhava‚Äî**

‚ÄúYou have been sent here by the Lord for pleasing His parents. Besides His parents, we do not see in this hamlet anything worth remembering for Him.‚Äù

‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§™‡•Ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡••

Uddhava‚Äî

‚ÄúOh, you are the persons whose objects are fulfilled, you are the persons worshipped by the (whole) world, you whose mind is thus offered to Lord Vasudeva.

‚Äò‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§§‡§™‡•ã‡§π‡•ã‡§Æ‡§ú‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡•ã‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•á ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••

‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§µ‡•É‡§£‡•Ä‡§§ ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§É‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúIt is devotion for for Krishna that is sought to be achieved by gifts, austerities, penance, oblations, the repeating of prayers, the studying of scriptures, self-control and other manifold paths to welfare. It is fortunate that you have sought the Supreme Being known as Krishna. Let the message from your beloved Lord which would bring you happiness, be heard.‚Äù

** ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî**

‚Äú‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§®‡•Å‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡§ö‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•á ‡§Æ‡§® ‡§Ü‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§® ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§ó‡•ã‡§ö‡§∞‡•á‡••

‚ÄúThe Lord says‚Äî

‚ÄòIf I, your beloved Lord, remain far away from your sight, it your sight, it is for drawing

your minds (to me) closer and for giving you continuous thought of Me. In the manner in which the mind remains absorbed when one‚Äôs dearest is far away, the mind of women does not remain absorbed, when (their dearest) is near and within sight.

‚Äú‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡•à‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡••‚Äù

** ‚ÄúMaking your minds completely absorbed in Me, you shall reach Me soon.‚Äù**

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•Ä‡§∞‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ã‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§ö‡•§
‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§•‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•å‡§ï‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Then, taking leave of the Gopis, Yasoda and Nanda, Uddhave returned to Mathura, protected by Krishna, and bowing to Him, informed Him of the heights of the devotion of the inhabitants of the Vraja.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734600952Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

‡§∞‡•Ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§£‡•Ä‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§É

KRISHNA MARRYING RUKMINI

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734601138Screenshot2024-12-15104407.png"/>

‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§ï‡§æ ‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§£‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§§‡•Ä‡••

There was a great king named Bhishmaka, the lord of the Vidarbhas. He had five sons and one virtuous daughter named Rukmini.

‡§∏‡•ã‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡•á ‡§∏‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Hearing of Krishna‚Äôs beauty, heroism, excellences and affluence sung by those who came to her house, Rukmini thought of Him as a suitable husband.

‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ç [‡§®‡•É‡§™]‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ü‡•ç ‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡••

When (all) the kinsmen desired to give his sister in marriage to Krishna, Rukmi (her eldest brother) who hated Krishna, prevented them from doing so, and considered (Sisupala), the king of the Chedis (as the proper husband).

‡§§‡§¶‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§≠‡•É‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Learning this, the dark-eyed Vidarbha princess, (Rukmini), became extremely dejected, (then) pondered (for a while), and quickly sent to Krishna a trustworthy Brahmin.

‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡••

Reaching Dvaraka¬πand led in by the door-keepers, the Brahmin saw the Prime Being, and described to Him everything.

‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ñ‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§•‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The Brahmin placed at Krishna‚Äôs feet the letter (of Rukmini) and bowed to Him. The Lord of the universe took it upand read it ardently.

__________________________________________________________________

1Dvaraka was an island in the sea, in the west of India, which Krishna had made his headquarters, after installing Ugrasena as king at Mathura.

‚Äú‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞ ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á
‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∞‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§ø‡§Æ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ñ‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠‡§Ç
‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á‡••

‚ÄúO! you who are most beautiful in the universe ! hearing of your excellences which, entering through the ears, remove the suffering of the body of those that hear of them, and of your beauty that is the realisation of all the desires of the eyes of those who are blessed with eyes, oh, Imperishable Lord! my mind unabashedly gets possessed by you.

‚Äò‡§ï‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§∂‡•Ä‡§≤‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™-
‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§£‡§ß‡§æ‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡§æ ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§® ‡§µ‡•É‡§£‡•Ä‡§§ ‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ
‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§®‡•É‡§∏‡§ø‡§Ç‡§π ‡§®‡§∞‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚Äú Which esteemed, intelligent and high-born maiden would not, in time, choose O! lion among men, Krishna! you who are her equalin birth, conduct, beauty,

learning, age, riches and power, and are a charm to the minds of the (whole) world of men?

‚Äò‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ-
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡•§
‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§§‡•Å ‡§ö‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç
‡§ó‡•ã‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§≤‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ú‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡••

‚ÄúTherefore, you have indeed been chosen by me as my husband and soul has been offered and my to you; make me now your own wife. O lotus-eyed Lord ! let not Sisupala come near and touch what is the portion of a hero, like a jackal the offering meant for a lion.

‚Äò‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡§®‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•ç
‡§ó‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•É‡§§‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ó‡§ß‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§¨‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§®‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§π ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•Å‡§≤‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúDuring my marriage that is to come off to-morrow, O! unconquered Lord ! come you secretly to the Vidarbhas, surrounded

by generals of armies, rout the forces of Sisupala and Jarasandha and by forcibly carrying me away, make me, away, make me, whose price is heroism, your wife.

‚Äò‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ
‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡§µ‡§ß‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúOn the day previous to the marriage, there is a grand procession to worship the patron goddess of the family, in which the new bride would come out and proceed to worship Parvati.

‚Äò‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ú‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑ ‡§® ‡§≤‡§≠‡•á‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ç
‡§®‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ï‡•É‡§∂‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§∂‡§§‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••‚Äù

‚ÄúO lotus-eyed Lord ! if I do not obtain your grace, I would (repeatedly) give up my life, delicate with austerities, through (even) a hundred births, if only I could. obtain your grace at the end.‚Äù

‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§§‡•Å ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•å‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§ó‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§ï‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡§ó‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§É‡••

Hearing the message of the Vidarbha princess, the scion of the Yadus and Sura mounted a chariot, took the Brahmin in it, and with swift horses, reached the Vidarbhas from the Anartas within a single night.

‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§∏ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§®‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§µ‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§∂‡§ø‡§∂‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡••

The king Bhishmaka, the Lord of Kundina19, being submissive to his love for his son, went about the necessary activities with a view to giving his daughter to Sisupala.

‡§Ü‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•å‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Adherents of Sisupala, the Paundrakas and others, the enemies of Krishna and Balarama, came in their thousands, ready prepared to secure the bride for Sisupala.

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§®‡•É‡§™‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•à‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§≤‡§π‡§∂‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§ú‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§•‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡••

Hearing of this effort of the enemy kings, and of Krishna having gone all alone to carry off the bride, and fearing a battle, Lord Balarama hastened to Kundina with elephants, horses, chariots and footmen.

‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ü‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§É ‡§≠‡§µ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

And the bride went from her apartments to the temple of the Mother, guarded by soldiers. Elderly Brahmin ladies, who knew the procedure, made that young lady bow to the auspicious goddess Bhavani, the spouse of the auspicious Siva.

** ‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§£‡•Ä‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§®‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§Ω‡§≠‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ã‡§¶‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

** Rukmini prayed to the goddess‚Äî**

‚ÄúMother! I bow incessantly to you, the auspicious goddess, in the company of your children. May Lord Krishna become my husband. May you approve of it.‚Äù

‡§Æ‡•å‡§®‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§Æ‡§• ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

Then, breaking her vow of silence with that, Rukmini came out of the temple of Ambika.

‡§™‡§¶‡§æ ‡§ö‡§≤‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§≤‡§π‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ç
‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç
‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The warriors who had come there became infatuated on seeing Rukmini of swan-like gait, walking. As that princess was mounting her chariot, Krishna carried her off, even as His enemies were looking on.

‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã‡§ó‡§Æ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡•à‡§É
‡§∂‡•É‡§ó‡§æ‡§≤‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡••

With his forces led by Rama, Krishna slowly went out of that gathering, even as a lion carrying off its portion would go out of the midst of jackals.

‡§™‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∞‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§ï‡§æ ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§É ‡§ú‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§æ‡§É‡••

Greatly perturbed, all the enemies chased Krishna, seizing their bows. (But), with their armies killed by the Vrishnis who were eager for victory, (those) kings led by Jarasandha turned back and went away.

‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§µ‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§Ø‡•á‡§Æ‡•á [‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§π]‡••

Conquering thus the (enemy) kings, the Lord brought the daughter of Bhishmaka to his city (Dvaraka), and married her in the prescribed manner.

_______

‡§®‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§µ‡§ß‡§É

THE KILLING OF NARAKASURA

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734618946Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§π‡•É‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡•å‡§Æ‡§ö‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ó‡§∞‡•Å‡§°‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§¢‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å‡••

Informed of the activities of (the demon) Bhauma20 by Indra whose emblem of sovereignty, the umbrella, had been carried away (by Bhauma), the Lord, mounting Garuda, went to the capital city of the Pragjyotishas along with his wife,(Satyabhama)21.

‡§™‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡§®‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∑‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§æ‡§® ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•å ‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ú‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

Hearing the sound of the Panchajanya (the Lord’s conch), dreadful like the thunder at the time of the aeon-end, the five-headed demon, Mura, who was sleeping, rose out of the waters.

‡§∂‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•å‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§¶‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§•‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§®‡§∞‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§™‡§æ‡§π‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∞‡§®‡•á‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡••

With (all) his efforts made futile, Bhauma seized his trident to kill the imperishable Lord. Even before he could aim it, Lord Hari took off, with His razor-edged discus, the head of Naraka, who was mounted on an elephant.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734604265Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

indifferent to wife as well as home; we remain full with self-realisation, and, like the on-looking light, ourselves devoid of any action.‚Äù

‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§≠‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ‡•§
‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§ò‡•ç‡§® ‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

Having said this much to Rukmini who was, on account of the absence of separation, regarding herself as the dearest of the Lord, the Lord, who desired to put an end to her pride, became silent.

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§ø ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡•á‡§™‡§•‡•Å‡§É
‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§π‡••

Hearing such unpleasant words, for the first time, from her beloved husband who was the Lord and Master of the three worlds, Rukmini became afraid in her heart, shuddered, wept and plunged into deep thought.

‡§§‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Æ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§®‡§æ [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§Ö‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§§‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§§‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

Seeing that strong attachment of His beloved, Lord Krishna, the refuge of the good, embraced with His arm that virtuous woman who knew none else (except her Lord), and consoled that poor Rukmini who deserved not those words.

** ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§•‡§æ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§® ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§®‡•á‡•§
‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∏‡•ç‡§´‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§ß‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

** The Lord‚Äî**

‚ÄúRukmini, do not get angry. I know you to be entirely devoted to Me. I did this in sport, lady, in my desire to hear your words and to see your face with its lip quivering in the agitation due to your love.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠‡•ã ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§ß‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∞‡•Å‡§≠‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúTimid and irascible lady ! Indeed, this is the greatest gain the house gives to householders, namely, the spending of the hours in pleasantries with the beloved.‚Äù

** ‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§£‡•Ä‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡§®‡§æ‡§π
‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡•ã ‡§®‡§®‡•Å ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§® ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç
‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§¨‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§≤‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§ú‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§π‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§® ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡•É‡§™‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¢‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§É
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¨‡§≤‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

** Rukmini‚Äî**

‚ÄúLotus-eyed Lord! Surely what you said is true; for I am not equal to the Lord who is limitless vastness. Surely, you are one who has no possession, you beyond whom there is nothing and to whom even those that receive offerings,

Brahma and others, bring their offerings! (True), those that are blinded with the sense of being rich, and those who gratify their own lives only, do not reach you who are the very end of everything. And you are dearest to the gods and they are dearest to you.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ú‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑ ‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§§‡•á ‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•Å ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúO lotus-eyed Lord! May I have devotion unto the feet of you who are revelling in your own self. That itself would be the greatest mercy shown to us.‚Äù

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734604539Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

‡§â‡§∑‡§æ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§Ø‡§É‚Äî

THE MARRIAGE OF ANIRUDDHA AND USHA

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734683855Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

‡§¨‡§æ‡§£‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§§‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•ã ‡§¨‡§≤‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§∂‡•ã‡§£‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•á ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§∏ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡••

There Was Bana, the eldest of the hundred sons of the great Bali22. In olden times, that Bana was rulingfrom the beautiful city named Sonita.

‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§§‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡•á‡§Ω‡§§‡•ã‡§∑‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É‡§°‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§∏ ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§™‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

With his thousand hands, Bana pleased Siva by providing instrumental music for His dance, and Siva persuaded him to accept a boon. Bana asked Him to be the guardian of his city.

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∑‡§æ ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§≤‡§≠‡§§ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§æ‡••

Bana‚Äôs daughter, a maiden, a maiden, Usha by name, had in a dream enjoyment with a lover (Aniruddha), the son of Kama, whom she had neither seen nor heard of before.

‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§≤‡•á‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡•§
‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡•ã‡§£‡§ø‡§§‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡••

Identifying that lover as Aniruddha, the son of Kama, Chitralekha, (Usha‚Äôs maid), resorted to her Yogic powers, brought Aniruddha to Sonitapura and showed the lover to her friend.

‡§ó‡•Ç‡§¢‡§É ‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•á ‡§∂‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§®‡§æ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡•á, ‡§¨‡§æ‡§£‡•ã‡§Ω‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä‡§¶‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Remaining concealed in in the maiden‚Äôs apartments, Aniruddha knew not the days passing, in the company of Usha, whose love had greatly increased. (But) Bana found out the scion of the Yadus23.

‡§§‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§ó‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§≤‡§ø‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•ã ‡§¨‡§≤‡•Ä
‡§ò‡•ç‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•à‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß ‡§π‡•§
‡§â‡§∑‡§æ ‡§≠‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§¶‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡§æ
‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§¶‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡••

The strong Bana, who was infuriated, bound with Nagapasa24 Aniruddha who had killed Bana‚Äôs forces. Hearing that Aniruddha had been bound, Usha became stricken with extreme sorrow and dejection, and wept with tears in her eyes.

‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ö‡•§
‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§æ‡§£‡§®‡§ó‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡§æ‡§É‡••

Hearing, from Narada, of the action of Aniruddha and the news of his capture the Sattvatta chiefs laid siege to the city of Bana.

‡§¨‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡•á ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É‡••

The terrible Lord, Siva, fought against Balarama and Krishna, for the sake of Bana.

‡§¨‡§æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§¢‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∞‡§®‡•á‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡•§
‡§ö‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§¶ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç ‡§∂‡§æ‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§É‡••

Mounting his chariot, Bana proceeded to fight Krishna. With His razor-edged discus, the Lord chopped off, like the branches of a tree, the arms of Bana, who was hurling missiles incessantly.

‚Äò‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§É‡•§‚Äô
‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§µ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúI gave the boon to Prahlada that his descendants were not to be killed by Me.‚Äù Thus obtaining security (from Lord Krishna), the demon, Bana, bowed to Krishna with his head, and brought to Him mounted in a chariot, Aniruddha together with the bride (Usha ).

‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•å‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§É‡§∏‡§Æ‡§≤‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ã‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

Placing in front Aniruddha with his wife, decked and dressed in beautiful garments, and surrounded by an Akshauhini of forces, Krishna went (to Dvaraka), with the approval of Siva.

‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç

KRISHNA’S HOUSEHOLD LIFE

‚Äî‚Äî‚Äîo‚Äî‚Äî‚Äî

‡§®‡§∞‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡§•‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§ï‡•á‡§® ‡§¨‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

Hearing that Naraka had been killed and that Krishna, a single individual, had married numerous women, the divine sage(Narada) came to see Him.

‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡•à‡§ï‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•å‡§∞‡•á‡§É ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡••

Narada entered one of the huge mansions of the wives of Krishna.

‡§™‡•Ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•å ‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡••

Krishna worshipped Narada with great love, by rising from His seat, by offering him a seat and by showing him similar honours, and asked him, as if He knew nothing, when he arrived.

‡§∏ ‡§§‡•Å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§ ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü ‡§ó‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∂‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç‡••

Wondering, Narada rose and silently went to another apartment and there also he saw Krishna, fondling His children.

‡§§‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á‡§Ω‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§è‡§ï‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•Å‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•å ‡§ö ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•á‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Then Narada saw Him in another apartment getting ready for ablution; in another, worshipping Sandhya and in silence, repeating the Gayatri; in one place, executing the sword-movements with sword and shield; lying on the bed and being extolled by minstrels somewhere, and holding consultations in some other place with Uddhava and other ministers; attending to Dharma in one place, to Artha and Kama in another, and in still another,

contemplating the one self, the Supreme Spirit that is beyond Matter.

‡§Ö‡§•‡•ã‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡§π‡•É‡§∑‡•Ä‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•§
‚Äò‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•á‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡••‚Äô

Narada then said smiling to the Lord of our faculties: ‚ÄúO Lord of Yoga! as a result of the worship of your feet, we are able to see these mystic manifestations of yours, appearing on the substratum (of yourself), though these are hard to be perceived by those whoare under the subjection of Illusion.‚Äù

** ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§§‡§¶‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ã‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡•§
‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ñ‡§ø‡§¶‡§É‡••‚Äô

** The Lord‚Äî**

‚ÄúO, you who have realised the soul ! I am the expounder of Dharma, its founder, and the person who commends it. And inculcating it, I am living in this world; be not distracted, my son.‚Äù

________

‡§ú‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡§ß‡§É‚Äî

THE KILLING OF JARASANDHA

‚Äî‚Äî‚Äîo‚Äî‚Äî‚Äî

** ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡§É‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§ñ‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ã‡§¶‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

** Narada‚Äî**

‚ÄúKing Yuddhishthira,¬π desirous of sovereignty, proposes to worship you with the Rajasuya, the greatest of the acrifices. May you approve of it.‚Äù

‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§Ç ‡§®‡•É‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§É‡••

Lord Krishna then issued orders for the journey (to Yudhishthira‚Äôs city). Hearing that the Lord, hard to be seen by men, had arrived, Yudhishthira, who was pleased,

__________________________________________________________________

  1. Yudhishthira, son of Pandu and Kunti, was Krishna‚Äôs aunt‚Äôs son. For the full account of the part Krishna played in the life and i the life and fortunes of the Pandavas, see the the Mahabharata. (G. A. Natesan & Co., G. T. Madras.)

went out (to receive Him) along with his preceptor and his friends.

‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•á‡§Ω‡§• ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É‡••

Yudhishthira then embraced, again and again, (their) most beloved (friend ) (Krishna), seen after a long time.

‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç
‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Æ‡§ú‡§¨‡§æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•å ‡§ï‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ü‡•Ä ‡§ö ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡§æ
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§Ω‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Smiling and with his senses in a flurry as a result of the force of his affection, Bhima embraced his uncle‚Äôs son (Krishna) and felt beatified; and the twins as well as Arjuna, with tears of joy swelling, joyously clasped their dearest friend, the imperishable Lord.

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§æ‡§≤‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§∏‡§Ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•à‡§∞‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡•á‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Thus, the Lord entered the decorated city along with His friends. Received by the people with great zeal. He entered the palace.

‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•á‡••

Seeing her nephew, Kunti rose up and embraced Him.

** ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•á‡§® ‡§ó‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•Ä‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã‡••‚Äô

** Yudhishthira‚Äî**

‚ÄúWith the Rajasuya, the greatest of sacrifices, I propose, Krishna, to worship the sanctifying manifestationsof yours. Lord, help us to perform it.‚Äù

** ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Ü‡§π‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

** The Lord‚Äî**

‚ÄúO king who routs his enemies ! well have you resolved. Vanquishing all kings, perform the great sacrifice.‚Äù

‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§´‡•Å‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ú‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•Ñ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ω‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§§ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Å‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡•ã‡§™‡§¨‡•É‡§Ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡••

Hearing the words of the Lord, Yudhishthira, with joyous face, set his brothers, made greater by by the the power of Lord Vishnu, to the task of conquering the quarters. (all) the quarters.

‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§ú‡§π‡•ç‡§∞‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§£‡§Ç [‡§®‡•É‡§™]‡••

Conquering the kings, the heroic (brothers) brought wealth.

‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§É ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ß‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§Ç [‡§§‡§æ‡§§] ‡§¨‡•É‡§π‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§§‡§É‡•§

Bhima, Arjuna and Krishna,‚Äîthese three, disguising themselves as Brahmins went to Girivraja25‚Äö the place where Jarasandha, the son of Brihadratha, was.

‡§§‡•á ‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡•§
‚Äò‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡•á‚Äô‡••

Approaching Jarasandha, the Kshatriyas, who were in Brahmin guise, begged of him: ‚ÄúKing, welfare unto you; give us what we desire.‚Äù

** ‡§ú‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§É‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§π‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§¶‡§¶‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§µ‡§É‡••‚Äô

** Jarasandha‚Äî**

‚ÄúBrahmins ! ask what you desire; I will give you even my head.‚Äù

** ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ï‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∏‡•å ‡§µ‡•É‡§ï‡•ã‡§¶‡§∞‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§π‡§ø ‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

** The Lord‚Äî**

‚ÄúWe are Kshatriyas who have come here seeking fight (with you), not expecting food. This is Bhima, this is his brother Arjuna, and know me as their uncle‚Äôs son, Krishna, your enemy.‚Äù

‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡§ß‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§π ‡§ö‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‚Äò‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§¶‡§¶‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§® ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á, ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã ‡§® ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡•ã ‡§® ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ, ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¨‡§≤‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§Æ‚Äô‡••

Thus informed, the king of the Magadhas laughed aloud, and said in anger: ‚ÄúFools ! I will then offer you battle. (Krishna!), I will not fight with you, a coward; neither my superior in strength nor my equal, Arjuna cannot fight me; Bhima is equal to me in strength.‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§¶‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡§ø‡§É‡••

Having spoken thus, Jarasandha gave Bhima a big mace, himself took another, and went out of the city.

‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§Æ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä‡§£‡§ú‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É [ ‡§®‡•É‡§™ ]‡••

The fight between the two of unabated force went on with victory for neither.

‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•Ä ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ò‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ü‡§™‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§ü‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§µ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

Lord Hari of unfailing insight, who knew how the enemy (Jarasandha) was born and how he would die26, infused Bhima with His own power, thought of the way to kill the enemy and showed to Bhima, by gesture, the tearing atwain of a branch.

‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§≤‡•á‡••

Understanding that, Bhima of great strength, the foremost of those who knew how to strike, caught the enemy by the feet, and threw him down on the ground.

‡§è‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§É‡•§
‡§ó‡•Å‡§¶‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§ü‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§∂‡§æ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§ó‡§ú‡§É‡••

Pressing one leg (of Jarasandha) with his foot, and snatching (Jarasandha’s) other leg with his arms, (Bhima) tore (Jarasandha) afwain, even as a great elephant might tear the bough of a tree.

‡§π‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§ó‡§ß‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•á‡•§
‡§∏‡§π‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ó‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ö‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡§ß‡•á‡§® ‡§Ø‡•á‡••

When the king of the Magadhas had been killed, there were hugeshouts of ‚ÄòHa ! Ha !‚Äô. The inscrutable Lord, the benefactor of all beings, anointed Sahadeva, the son the son of Jarasandha, as the king of the Magadhas, and released (all) the kings whohad been imprisoned by Jarasandha.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734879444Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

‡§∂‡§ø‡§∂‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§µ‡§ß‡§É‚Äî

THE KILLING OF SISUPALA

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734879540Screenshot2024-11-03140300.png"/>

‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§ú‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ò‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏ ‡§ã‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§É‡•§
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§É‡•§
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•Å‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡•à‡••

Hearing of the killing of Jarasandha, king (Yudhishthira) invited the priests (for the sacrifice). All the kings and queens who were invited came (to attend) the Rajasuya (sacrifice) of king Yudhishthira.

‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡§ï‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§∏‡§É‡••

Priests, lustrous like the gods, made the sovereign (Yudhishthira) perform the sacrifice.

‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ω‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§®‡•Ä‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡•ã ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§≠‡§æ‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•É‡§∑‡•Ä‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§≤‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§É‡••

On the day of the offering of the Soma juice, the king ascertained the intention of those in the assembly and offered worship to Lord Krishna. All the people folded their hands in respect.

‡§¶‡§Æ‡§ò‡•ã‡§∑‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä ‚Äò‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•Ä‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§§‡§ø‚Äô‡•§
‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§¨‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡•á ‡§®‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§≤‡§É‡••

‚ÄúA cowherd and a blot on his family, one living a reckless life and bereft of all good qualities, how does Krishna deserve honour ?‚Äù These and similar unhappy words, did the irate Sisupala, son of Damaghosha, utter, his good fortune coming to an end.

‡§§‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§ú‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á ‡§ñ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•Ä‡•§
‡§≠‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§¶‡§∏‡§ø [ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§ ]‡••

Then the Chedi king (Sisupala) calmly seized his sword and armour, condemning the kings in the assembly who had taken the side of Krishna.

‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡•§
‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡•ã‡§É‡•§

Rising up in the meantime, the Lord drew aside His friends, and in His anger, severed with His razor-edged discus, the head of the enemy (Sisupala) who rushed at Him.

‡§ö‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∞‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•ã‡§π‡§ø ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The effulgence that arose out of the body of the king of the Chedis became one with Lord Vasudeva. Thinking intensely (of the Lord) with a mind overwhelmed by the accumulated enmity of three births, he attained the form of the Lord. For, indeed, mental absorption (in a thing) makes one take its form.27

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•å‡§≠‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡•à‡§É‡••

Similarly, the Lord killed the Saubha king Salva, Dantavaktra27with his younger brother, and other insufferable kings, and was extolled by the gods and men.

_______

‡§ï‡•Å‡§ö‡•á‡§≤‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç ‚Äî

THE STORY OF KUCHELA

‚Äî‚Äî:o:‚Äî‚Äî

‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§¶‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Ä‡••

There was a friend of Krishna, a Brahmin, foremost of those who have realised the Brahman, unattracted to objects of pleasure, of tranquil mind and subdued senses, a householder who was living by what came unsought.

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§ö‡•á‡§≤‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡•§
‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§¶‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§æ‡••

The devoted wife of that Kuchela, who was emaciated with hunger, but was of the same nature (as her husband), told her husband with a withered face:

‚Äò‡§®‡§®‡•Å ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡•à‡§π‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§£‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∞‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§®‡•á‡••

‚ÄúO Brahmin ! is not the Lord of the Goddess of Fortune Himself a friend of your adored self ? O self ? O you who are blessed ! approach Him, the refuge of the good. He will give ample wealth to you who are perishing with a large family.‚Äù

‡§∏ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§∂‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•Å‡§É ‡•§
‚Äò‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠ ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‚Äô‡•§
‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ß‡•á ‡••

Thus entreated many times, softly, by his wife, the Brahmin thought: ‚ÄúThis indeed is the greatest gain, the seeing of the Lord of purest fame.‚Äù And he decided to go (to the Lord).
