‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Å‡§ï‡§§‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•Å‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§ö‡•á‡§≤‡§ñ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•á‡§® ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡••

Begging of (the neighbouring) Brahmins four handfuls of Prithuka (fried and Rattened rice), and tying them in a piece of cloth, Kuchela proceeded to Dwaraka,thinking: ‚ÄúHow can I have the sight of Krishna !‚Äù

‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡•à‡§ï‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡••

Kuchela entered one of the mansions of Krishna feeling like one who had attained beatitude.

‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ö‡§•‡•ã‡§™‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§¨‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§â‡§™‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•å ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§Æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡••

The imperishable Lord saw Kuchela, approached and embraced him with joy. Seating him then on a cot, the Lord Himself fetched things for the worship of the friend, washed his feet and spoke words of welcome.

‡§ï‡•Å‡§ö‡•á‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä ‡§ö‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡•à‡••

Queen Rukmini attended with the chowrie upon that untidy, emaciated Brahmin, Kuchela, who had a body only of veins and nerves.

‡§ï‡§•‡§Ø‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§•‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡•á ‡§∏‡§§‡•ã‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§≤‡§≤‡§ø‡§§‡§æ [ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ] ‡§ï‡§∞‡•å ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Clasping each other‚Äôs hands, Krishna and Kuchela talked their own beautiful old stories (of the days ) when they were in the teacher‚Äôs house together.

** ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§§‡•á ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡•§
‡§®‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ß‡§®‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á‡••

** The Lord‚Äî**

‚ÄúIn household life, life, your mind is not lost in material desires. O man of wisdom ! I know you are not over-fond of riches.

‚Äò‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§£‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§π‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Æ‡•ç‡§£‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§™‡§π‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•á‡••

‚ÄúO Brahmin ! What offering have you brought for me from your house ? Even the little that is offered by the devoted will become ample because of the love; and even the ample that is offered by the unloving does not suffice to satisfy Me.

‚Äò‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§Ç ‡§´‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ã‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§§‡§¶‡§π‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§ ‡§™‡§π‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúA leaf, a flower, a fruit, or some water,‚Äîif one gives me any of these in devotion, I enjoy that offering of devotion from one of pure soul.‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§§‡§Ø‡•á ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Å‡§ï‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç [ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ] ‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§¶‡§µ‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§É‡••

Though he was told in this manner, the Brahmin, ashamed and with a down-cast face, did not give the handful of Prithuka to Krishna who was the Lord of the goddess of wealth.

‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¶‡•É‡§ï‡•ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ú‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡••

‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§≤‡§≠‡§æ‡§É‡••

Understanding the cause of Kuchela‚Äôs visit, the Lord, who is the witness of the souls of all beings, thought: ‚ÄúThis Kuchela never worshipped me in the past, desiring wealth. It is to please his devoted wife that my friend has come now; I will give him riches hard to be cbtained even by the gods.‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§∞‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Å‡§ï‡§§‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•Å‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡••

Thinking thus, the Lord Himself snatched from the Brahmin‚Äôs garment the Prithuka tied in a rag, asking him: ‚ÄúWhat is this?‚Äù

‚Äò‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Å‡§ï‡§§‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•Å‡§≤‡§æ‡§É‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúFriend, you have brought me this, which pleases me most. These grains of Prithuka will indeed satisfy me who am of the form of the Universe.‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§π‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§¶‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡•§
‚Äò‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ω‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡•á‚Äô‡••

Saying this, the Lord ate one handful, and took a second handful to eat. Ere He ate, goddessLakshmi (Rukmini) caught in haste the hand of the lord saying: ‚ÄúThis (one handful) suffices, O Lord who is of the form of the universe ! to fill one with all the riches.‚Äù

‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§∞‡§ú‡§®‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡•§
‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§Ç [ ‡§§‡§æ‡§§ ] ‡§™‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

The Brahmin lived that night in the mansion of the imperishable Lord and the next morning, saluted by the Lord, the bestower of prosperity to the universe, and accompanied by Him for some distance, went home, pleased.

‡§∏ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ß‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§§‡•Å ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§É‡••

Not receiving any riches from Krishna, Kuchela did not ask for them himself. He went home ashamed, but happy at having seen the great Lord.

‚Äò‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§∞‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§§‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ß‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§® ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§ø‡§ï‡•ã ‡§®‡•Ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§® ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∞‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§‚Äô
‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§ú‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§É‡•§

‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡§µ‡§®‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•à‡§É ‡§ï‡•Ç‡§ú‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§ú‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡••

‚ÄúWhere am I, a pauper and a sinner and where is Krishna, the abode of the Goddess of Fortune? He embraced me with his arms because I was born a Brahmin. The worship of His feet is the source of all of all attainments. The merciful Lord, I am sure, did not give me ample wealth, thinking that, obtaining wealth, this poor self of mine might get intoxicated and forget Him.‚Äù Thus thinking within himself, Kuchela approached the vicinity of his home, which was (now) surrounded on all sides by storied mansions bright like the sun, fire and moon, and wonderful wonderful parks and gardens full of bevies of warbling birds, and inhabited by beautifully decked men and fawn-eyed women.

‚Äò‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§§‡§¶‡§ø‡§¶‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡•§‚Äô
‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§®‡§∞‡§æ ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Æ‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§≠‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ‡••

‚ÄúWhat is this ? Whose abode is this ? How did this come to be ?‚Äù As he was thus thinking, god-like men and women received that blessed Kuchela with tumultuous music.

‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ω‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡•§
‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§≤‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ß‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•á‡••

Hearing that her husband had come, the wife (of Kuchela), with exhilaration and in a flurry, closed her eyes, eyes, bowed to him with her mind, and embraced him with her heart.

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∂‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡•á‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡••

Being pleased, Kuchela, along with his wife, entered his abode, having hundreds of jewelled pillars and looking like great Indra’s abode.

‚Äò‡§®‡•Ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§§‡•à‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø
‡§∂‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡§ñ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§µ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã
‡§®‡•à‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúFor this prosperity coming to me, unfortunate and eternally poor, surely there can can be no other cause than my seeing the best of the Yadus, the Lord who is the great boundless‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§§‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•á‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§¨‡•Å‡§≠‡•Å‡§ú‡•á ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§ü‡§É‡••

Making up his mind thus and becoming an (ever more) intense devotee of the Lord, Kuchela, with his wife, enjoyed (all) pleasures, not hankering too much after them but with a view to (gradually) renounce them.

‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§É‚Äî

ADVICE TO UDDHAVA

‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡§≤‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Having killed the demons, with (the aid of) Balarama and the Yadus, Krishna relieved Earth of her burden by creating the mutual quarrel which would quicken destruction.

‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ï‡•ã‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¨‡§π‡•Å ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•Å‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•à‡§É
‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§π‡•á‡§≤‡§®‡§ï‡§ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§∞‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç
‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§π‡§∞‡§§‡•ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∂‡§É‡••

Taking as ostensible cause the sons of Pandu, who were provoked in the extreme by their enemies deceitful gambling, mocking, seizure of their queen by the hair and the rest, Krishna made the kings who had assembled (on the battle-field ) kill each other, and (thus) removed Earth‚Äôs burden.

‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§∂‡§∞‡§∂‡§§‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§§ ‡§ó‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

Then, Brahma, along with Siva and the gods, extolled Lord Hari and saluting Him, addressed Him from the skies:

‚Äò‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã‡•§
‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡•à‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúLord, we once petitioned you to remove Earth‚Äôs burden and you, the soul of everything, have done accordingly.

‚Äò‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúAnd you have also (firmly) established Dharma among the good and the truthful. Hence, if you think So, enter your own supreme effulgence.‚Äù

** ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ñ‡§ø‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§¶‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§µ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ø‡§ò‡•É‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á. ‡§µ‡•á‡§≤‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§µ‡§É‡•§

‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•É‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§≤‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‚Äô

** The Lord‚Äî**

‚ÄúYour work has been done ; Earth‚Äôs burden has been removed. (But) this race of the Yadavas, haughty with an excess of heroism and valour, desires to engulf the world but is held in restraint by Me, as the great ocean by the shore. If I go away without ending this vast race of haughty Yadus, this world will perish at the hands of this race which would transgress (all) bounds.‚Äù

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§π ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡••

Then, noticing grave evil portents appearing in Dvaraka, the Lord told the Yadu elders, who had gathered:

‚Äò‡§® ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúElders ! if we desire life, we must not live here; we shall go away to the sacred Prabhasa forthwith; tarry not.‚Äù

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡§®‡•§
‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡•ã [ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ] ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§ ‡§â‡§™‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§≤‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§§‡••

Thus commanded by the Lord, (the Yadavas) made ready their chariots. Seeing them get ready, get ready, Uddhava, ever devoted to Krishna, approached the overlord of the universe in solitude, bowed with his head at his feet, and said to Him with folded hands:

‡§∏‡§Ç‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§®‡•Ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‚Äò‡§®‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡§Æ‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§µ‡•§
‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡•á ‡§®‡§æ‡§• ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§®‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúAfter bringing toan end this race, surely you will leave this world altogether. My Lord, I cannot leave off your lotusfeet even for a fraction of a second; take me also to your place.‚Äù

** ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ω‡§π‡•ç‡§®‡§•‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••

** The Lord‚Äî**

‚ÄúThe work of the gods on this earth has been completed by Me. And this city, the sea will flood on the seventh day (from now).

‚Äò‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§ï‡§≤‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§® ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ‡•á‡§π ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§≤‡•á‡••

‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡§®‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§∑‡•Å‡•§
‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ô‡§ó‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúSoon, the world will be rendered evil by Kali. You must not live in the world abandoned by Me. Casting off all your attachment for your your kith kith and kin, and fastening your mind well on Me, wander about the earth, with an equanimous mind.

‚Äò‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•á‡••

‚ÄúWith your senses and mind in concentration, see the universe as projected out of your own soul and soul and your soul as projected out of Myself, the Overlord.

** ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡§É‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï ‡§Æ‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§¶‡•É‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã‡••‚Äô

** Uddhava‚Äî**

‚ÄúO Lord of highest fame ! of what nature is the good man according to you?‚Äù

** ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî**

‚Äò‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡•Å‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§É ‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•à‡§∞‡§π‡§§‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•Å‡§É ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§¶‡§É ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§É ‡§Æ‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§ø‡§ï‡§É ‡§ï‡§µ‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‚Äò‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ú‡•á‡§§ ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§É‡••

** The Lord‚Äî**

‚ÄúUnable to bear another’s suffering, unharmful and folbearing towards all beings; one whose strength is Truth, who is irreproachable, equanimous, helpful

to all; of mind unspoilt by desires, selfpossessed, mild, pure, owning nothing; not expecting honour from others, ready to honour all, efficient, the very embodiment of friendliness and impelled to act act by compassion alone; one of noble vision and one who, transcending all Dharmas, worships Me, he is indeed the greatest man.

‚Äò‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É‡§∏‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§¶‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç
‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∏‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡§ú ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§ö
‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••

‚ÄúOnly by devotion and faith can I, who am the Soul and thus the beloved, be grasped by the good. Devotion firmly established towards Me sanctifies even a born Chandala. Chandala. He whose voice falters, whose heart melts, who sheds tears often

and laughs sometimes, and without any shame sings aloud and dances‚Äîhe. My devotee, purifies the (whole) universe.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§π‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§É‡••

‚ÄúUddhava, I am the soul, the friend and the master of all these beings; I am all beings; I am their birth, existence and death.

‚Äò‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§¨‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡•Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§® ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§® ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ã‡§ü‡§ø‡§∂‡§É‡••

‚ÄúOf worships, I am the worship of the knowledge of the Brahman. Of vows, I am the vow of non-injury. Among Dharmas, I am the giving of security to all. Among varieties of safety, ‘I am inwardness of mind. I am the patience of the patient and the goodness of the good. I can in

time count the atoms but not the glorious manifestations of Myself who am creating worlds by crores.

‚Äò‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§π‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•å‡§≠‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç‡§Ω‡§∂‡§ï‡§É‡••

‚ÄúEffulgence, Beauty, Fame, Lordship,the sense of Shame in doing wrong, Sacrifice, Auspiciousness, Fortune, Heroism, Forbearance, Wisdom,‚Äîwhatever possesses these is a manifestation of Myself.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§π‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§≤‡•ã‡§≠‡§§‡§æ‡•§
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§π‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§ø‡§ï‡§É‡••

‚ÄúNon-injury, Truthfulness, Non-thieving, absence of Passion, Anger and Avarice, striving to do what is pleasing and beneficial to beings‚Äîthese are Dharmas common to all castes.

‚Äò‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§®‡•É‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ö ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§®‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§•‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúDesirous of doing good to humanity, I have expounded three yogas: Knowledge, Action and Devotion; there is no other path anywhere.

‚Äò‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§® ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§£‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§¶‡§É‡••

‚ÄúThe path of Knowledge is for those who have cultivated indifference to material objects; the path of Action is for those who have still Desire; for him who is not yet thoroughly indifferent but is not also too much attached, the path of Devotion bears fruit.

‚Äò‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§ ‡§® ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡•§
‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§•‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§£‡§æ‡§¶‡•å ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••

‚ÄúOne should be performing Acts only so long as he has not attained Indifference, or only so long as Faith in listening to My story and similar acts of devotion has not been produced.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡§ò‡§É ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

‚ÄúRemaining in the midst of this world, one who abides by his Dharma, commitsnosin and is pure, easily attains pure wisdom or devotion to Me.

‚Äò‡§®‡•à‡§∞‡§™‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡§®‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúNon-expectation of anything is said to be the greatest and amplest bliss.

‚Äò‡§Ø ‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§•‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§≤‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•á‡••

‚ÄúThose who leave these paths of Devotion, Knowledge and Action leading to Me, and enjoy mean pleasures with their fickle lives, migrate from birth to birth.

‚Äò‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ω‡§®‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡•á‡§¶‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§É ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡•§
‡§è‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§®‡•É‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúTheft, Injury, Falsehood, Hypocrisy, Desire, Anger, Conceit, Infatuation, Making distinctions, Enmity, Distrust, Rivalry, Addiction to the three vices of woman, wine and gambling‚Äîthese fifteen evils of men are considered as having their root in wealth.

‚Äò‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ
‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§è‡§∑‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§£
‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§§‡§Æ‡§∏‡§ø ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡••

‚ÄúMistaking as ‚ÄòMine and I‚Äô this body which is but a product a product of the of the mind, blinded men say in their illusion ‚ÄòThis is myself, this is another‚Äô, and wander in the limitless dark.

‚Äò‡§™‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•á‡§£ ‡§ö‡••

‚ÄúRealising the universe as one, both in Matter and Spirit, one should neither praise nor condemn the character and actions of others.

‚Äò‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§®‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

‚ÄúWith his mind offered to Me, with his mind and soul revelling in Dharmas leading to Me, one, should do all acts for My sake, calmly and with My thought.

‚Äò‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§¨‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§™‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§à‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§ñ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ø‡§É‡••

‚ÄúWith a pure mind, one should see Me, who am uncovered by anything, as established within and without all beings, as the supreme spirit in his own self, like the (all-pervading) ether.

‚Äò‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§∏‡§≠‡§æ‡§ú‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

‚ÄúThus, O resplendent Uddhava, taking his stand on pure knowledge, he should consider all beings as Myself and honour them.

‚Äò‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§≤‡•ç‡§ï‡§∏‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•á ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§´‡•Å‡§≤‡§ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ï‡•á‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•á ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§¶‡•É‡§ï‡•ç ‡§™‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§§‡§É‡••

‚ÄúHe is the learnedman who realises the same Me in the Brahmin as well as the Chandala, in the thief as well as the person who is versed in the Vedas, in the sun as well as in a spark, in the good as well as in the cruel.

‚Äò‡§®‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ã ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§π‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡§ø‡••

‚ÄúFrom n the person who incessantly contemplates the Me in all all men, quickly do rivalry, jealousy, contempt and egotism flee.

‚Äò‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§°‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§¶‡•à‡§π‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•å ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§æ‡§≤‡§ó‡§æ‡•ã‡§ñ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúLaying aside his pride, prestige and shame, and also the sense of the physical differences, one should prostrate himself on the ground, like a stick, before all beings down to the dog, the Chandala, the bull and the ass.

‚Äò‡§è‡§∑‡§æ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Æ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§É ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§∑‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•É‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•á‡§π ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúThis is the knowledge of the knowing and the wisdom of the wise that, with the unreal and mortal, (body), man attains to Me, the Real and the Immortal.

‚Äò‡§®‡•à‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§∏‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§µ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§™‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••‚Äù

‚ÄúHaving known this, the inquirer has nothing more left to know. To him who has drunk of ambrosia, there is nothing else remaining to be drunk.‚Äù

‡§∏ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§É
‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§≤‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§É
‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•Ä‡§™‡§É‡••

Having been shown thus the path to union with God, Uddhava folded his hands in respect and told the great hero of the Yadus: ‚Äú(All) the darkness of my delusion has been driven away; indeed, the light of Knowledge has been given to me.‚Äù

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äî

‚Äò‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø ‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

** The Lord‚Äî**

‚ÄúUddhava, go you on my command to Mine own hermitage named Badari. There contemplate in solitude what you have been taught. And with your speech and mind completely absorbed in Me, you shall reach Me.‚Äù

‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø
‡§ó‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡§¶‡•á‡§ï‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§®‡§æ
‡§§‡§™‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§π‡§∞‡•á‡§∞‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Then, establishing the Lord within his heart, the great devotee of the Lord (Uddhava) went to Badari and, performing penance,attained to the state of Lord Hari as taught to him by (Himself), the one Friend of the universe.

‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‚Äî

THE PASSAGE OF THE LORD28

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734919484Screenshot2024-11-03140300.png"/>

‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§•‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡•å‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•Ç ‡§∞‡§•‡•à‡§É‡••

Seeing ominous portents appearing in the heavens, skies and on earth, and hearing what Krishna told them, all the Yadu elders acquiesced, crossed the sea on boats and reached Prabhasa on their chariots

‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡•§
‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

Then, at Prabhasa, the Yadavas who lost their senses through Fate, drank the powerful drink, the liquor called Maireyaka, whereby one’s senses are lost.

‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡•Å‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∞‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§É ‡§µ‡•á‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡••

A great quarrel arose among them who were intoxicated with excessive drink. Desiring to kill each other, the infuriated Yadavas fought on the sea-shore.

‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§≠‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§¶‡•å‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§É
‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡§®‡•ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§¢‡§æ‡§É‡••

Sons fought with tathers, brothers, nephews, grandsons, and uncles ; friends fought friends, and besotted, kinsmen killed kinsmen.

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡•á‡§Ω‡§µ‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

When all His clans had thus perished, the Lord, who who remained, thought that Earth’s burden had been removed.

‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•á‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡•å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡••

On the sea-shore, Rama sat in Yogic contemplation of the Supreme Being, united His soul with the universal soul, and left the mortal world.

‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Seeing the passage of Balarama, the Lord who incarnated Himself as the son of Devaki, sat in silence on the ground and entered His own abode.

‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø ‡§¶‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§≠‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡•á‡§¶‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡•á‡§§‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§É ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•Å ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É‡••

Drums rumbled in the heavens and from the skies, flowers fell. Truth, Righteousness, Self-possession, Fame and Fortune went away from Earth along with Him.

‡•• ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§•‡§æ ‡••

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734920007Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>
THUS ENDS THE STORY OF THE
INCARNATION AS KRISHNA.

‡•• ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É‡••

‡•• ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§•‡§æ ‡••

THE STORY OF THE INCARNATION AS KALKI

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734928397Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§®‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§™‡§•‡•á ‡§®‡•É‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡§æ‡§ñ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•Å‡§∞‡•á ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•Å‡•§
‡§ö‡•å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•É‡§§‡§µ‡•É‡§•‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å ‡§µ‡•à ‡§®‡•É‡§∑‡•Å‡•§
‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§≤‡•å ‡§ó‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ú‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•Å ‡§ñ‡§∞‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§£‡§ø‡•§
‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••

When the Dharma of those that observe the Varna and Asrama is lost, when the Vedic path of men has disappeared, when Dharma has become predominantly heretic, when rulers have become more or less thieves, when men are living through the various means of theft, falsehood and wanton violence to others, when the Kali29 agehas thus well-advanced towards the end, when man is essentially violent in nature, the Lord will incarnate Himself with His goodness, purity and knowledge, for saving Dharma.

‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§≤‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Å‡§Ø‡§∂‡§∏‡§É ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••

The Lord will manifest Himself as Kalki in the house of Vishnuyasas, a high-souled Brahmin, chief of those in the village of Sambhala.

‡§Ö‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§≤‡§ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§¶‡•ã ‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡•ã‡§ü‡§ø‡§∂‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••

Riding a fleet steed, Devadatta, the Lord of the Universe will slay by crores the thieves in the guise of rulers.

‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ω‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡••

When Hari, the Lord of Dharma, incarnates Himself as Kalki, there will be the Krita age and men will be born with goodness, purity and knowledge.

‡•• ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§•‡§æ ‡••

THUS ENDS THE STORY OF THE
INCARNATION AS KALKI.

‡•• ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡••

THE SALVATION OF PARIKSHIT

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734928811Screenshot2024-12-15104407.png"/>

‚Äò‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ‡§è‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§®‡§∞‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡•§
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•å ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡••

‚ÄúKing Parikshit ! I have spoken of these, kings as well as others, who took Earth as their own, but who left Her and died.

‚Äò‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ú‡§Ø‡•á ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§π‡§∏‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‚Äú‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§ó‡•Ä‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§®‡§ï‡§æ ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§É‡••

‚ÄúSeeing kings feverishly busy to conquer Her, this Earth laughs: ‚ÄòAlas ! (these ) kings, playthings of Death, desire to conquer Me !

‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§Ø‡•á ‡§´‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äù

‚ÄòWhat is this conquest of territory before the conquest of spirit ? Deliverance is the fruit of the conquest of spirit.‚Äô

‚Äò‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å ‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•å ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúTherefore, O king, fix Hari in your heart by every means. With your mind in concentration, you who are about to die, shall thereby attain to the supreme goal.

‚Äò‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§∂‡•Å‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§π‡§ø‡•§
‡§ò‡§ü‡•á ‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂ ‡§Ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡•§
‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡•á ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•á ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É‡••

‚ÄúKing, cast away the thought that you are about to die, a thought which only the being that has not risen above its body can have. Even as when a pot is broken, the ether that was within it becomes the (common) ether without as before, so also when the body dies, the individual spirit becomes the universal spirit.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§π‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡§≤‡•á‡•§
‡§¶‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•á‡§≤‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§® ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡••‚Äô

‚Äú‚ÄòI am the supreme spirit, the supreme effulgence; the Brahman is myself; I am the supreme goal.‚Äô With this know. ledge and with your spirit placed on the unconditioned spirit, you will not perceive Takshaka biting your foot or licking it with poisonous tongues, or this body or this universe. as separate from your spirit.‚Äù

‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‚Äî

‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡•§
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§®‡•ã ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É‡••

** King Parikshit‚Äî**

‚ÄúI have realised my object; I have been graced by your merciful self by making me hear of Hari Himself, the Lord without beginning or end.

‚Äò‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç ‡§§‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ï‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•á‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

‚ÄúLord, I am not afraid not afraid of death from Takshaka or others. I have entered the Bliss which is the Brahman. You have shown me that thing on realisingwhich fear ceases to exist.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§π‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ú‡•á‡•§
‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúGive me leave, O you who have realised the Brahman ! I shall subdue the expression of all the senses; and making my mind, cleared of even the vestiges of yearnings, enter the Lord, I shall give up my life.‚Äù

** ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§§‡§É‚Äî**

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¨‡§æ‡§¶‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§®‡§∞‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡•Ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

** The Suta‚Äî**

Thus told and honoured by king Parikshit, the worshipful son of Vyasa, Suka gave him leave and departed along with (other) ascetics.

‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§¶‡§™‡§ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡•§
‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§§‡§∞‡•Å‡§É‡••

And the royal sage Parikshit placed his mind with his intellect on the Inner Light, and with his breath still, contemplated, looking like a (motionless) tree.

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§ï‡•Ç‡§≤‡•á ‡§¨‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã ‡§ó‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§ï‡•Ç‡§≤‡•á ‡§â‡§¶‡§ô‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§É‡•§
‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§É, ‡§§‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ï‡•ã ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§¶‡§∂‡§¶‡•ç, ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§ø‡§ó‡§∞‡§≤‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡•§
‡§¨‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ ‡§≠‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Bereft of all attachments, Parikshitsaton thethe bank of the Ganges facing the north, on sacred grass placed eastward, and becoming a great yogin, passed the Brahman. The (serpent) Takshaka stungthe king; and passed into even as all the people were looking on, the body of the royal sage who had become the Brahman became a heap of ashes as a result result of the fire of the snake’s poison.

‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§≠‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡•á‡§¶‡•Å‡§É ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§∏‡•ã ‡§ú‡§ó‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§É‡••

Heavenly drums rumbled; the Gandharvas and the celestial damsels sang and applauding (Parikshit), the gods sent showers of flowers.

‡•• ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡••

THUS ENDS THE STORY OF THE SALVATION
OF PARIKSHIT

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734928029Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

‡§®‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§†‡§Æ‡•á‡§ß‡§∏‡•á ‡•§
‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Obeisance unto that divine Vyasa of unfailing intellect, by the contemplation of whose lotus-feet, I learnt this sacred text (of the Bhagavata).

‡§¶‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••

He who extends (to others) (the benefit of) the Bhagavata, attains the supreme goal. The glorious Bhagavata is the essence of all the Upanishads.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734928029Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>
‡•• ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡••

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734928029Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>
THUS ENDS THE BHAGAVATA

THE BHAGAVATA

BY

DR. V. RAGHAVAN, M.A., Ph.D.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734925347Screenshot2024-12-15104840.png"/>

–¢HE Purana is a reinforcement (Upabrihmana) of the teachings of the Vedas, with arguments for God and Dharma in the form of accounts of the creation, the sages, and the lives of the kings of the past. This is the real meaning of the traditional definition of the Purana as ‚ÄòPanchalakshana‚Äô. The supremacy of the Lord and Dharma is made the more explicit purpose of the Purana in the amplified ‚ÄòDasalakshana‚Äô (ten characteristics) given by the Bhagavata (II. 10. 1-7). The Lord, as Asraya, is given as the chief of these ten features of the Purana and along with this are introduced as definite subjects the stories of the incarnations which the Lord took for the re-establishment of His Kingdom and for the renaissance of Dharma on earth, and Salvation (Mukti). The first nine subjects only qualify the tenth, the Asraya, and are intended to strengthen it. (Dasamasya visuddhyartham navanamiha lakshanam. II. 10.2). In this, the Bhagavata shifts the emphasis from Principle to

Personality. The same emphasis on the Personality of the Lord is effectively laid in the preliminary story of the genesis of the Bhagavata, of how Vyasa, at the instance of Narada, composed the Bhagavata for singing exclusively of the Lord’s glories and thus removing the depressing emptiness of his heart which he felt even after his composing the great Mahabharata and the other Puranas. The very name of the Purana shows that it is the lays of the Lord par excellence.

Of the Principles, Dharma, Jnana and Vairagya, the Lord Himself is the embodiment. Devotion, Bhakti, to the Personality, the Lord, is to be achieved and its achievement means and includes the Principles also. Knowledge, Action, and Devotion‚ÄîJnana, Karma, Bhakti‚Äîas envisaged by the Bhagavata are neither exclusive of each other nor contradictory. To know truly is to is to love Him; and Devotion can be of the best form only when it is informedby Knowledge. Knowledge and Love must express themselves in Acts of Devotion. But the Lord seems to say in His discourse to Uddhava that the path of Devotion is the best for us, for it is suited to those who are attached to various interests in life on earth and yet have some spiritual yearnings. This seems to be the meaning of the saying that Bhakti is the path for the

Kali age. It is an age in which emotion is dominant; it is its spiritual harnessing that is Bhakti. And this has been woven into an allegorical story on the greatness of the Bhagavata, the Bhagavata Mahatmya, found in the Padma Purana.

Two of the problemsfacing the reader of the Bhagavata are the salvation of those that hate the Lord and wreck His Kingdom, and the story of the sports of Krishna with the women of the Gokula. In the stories of the demons, the Asuras and the Rakshasas, the Purana tackles the problem of evil (VII. 1. 1-3). The Asura is called a Purvadeva: the demon was a god; the being that is inherently and originally divine, errs and is, and is, through the story of a curse, made to be born as a demoniac force disturbing the peace of Dharma. The Asura or Rakshasa hates the Lord intensely and incessantly to hasten the time of the Lord’s appearance to put an end to his evil self and to restore him to his original state. Death at the Lord’s hands is invariably attended with the grant of salvation. This is nade plain in the story of Jaya and Vijaya, which lies at the very basis of the work.

Of the Love which the individual soul, caught in the meshes of a distracting world, is expected to develop for the Lord, the noblest image that has

occurred to the mystics of all religions is the Love of woman for man. The intensity and the fight against odds that this God-love means find find a parallel only in clandestine love. Hence the saying: Yosha jaramiva priyam. The mystic language of the Rasa is hardly stranger than that of Solomon’s song of songs, or of St. Bernard’s sermons, or of the writings of Coventry Patmore, which speak of Christ the bridegroom and Church the bride. ‚ÄúThe Law and the Prophets describe pure by impure. Bride and Bridegroom are the highest images.‚Äù ‚ÄúThy maker is Thy Husband.‚Äù That the Lord’s dance with the cowherd women and their Love for Him mean something which has to be sought beyond their face-meaning must be very clear to anybody. For the Lord Himself tells the women when they seek Him: ‚ÄúThe Love of those whose minds are absorbed in Me cannot be physical love: Na mayyavesitadhiyam kamah kamaya kalpate.‚Äù (X. A. 22-26.)

PRIYAVRATA. **‚Äî**A son of Manu. See footnote on p. 81.; is endowed with an element of the Lord.

**SATRUGHNA.‚Äî**Brother of Rama; partial manifestation of the Lord; fourth son of Dasaratha; celebrated in the Ramayana.

**SATVATA.‚Äî**A tribe related to the Yadavas.

**SATYAVRATA.‚Äî**A southern king, a devotee of the Lord; the Lord appears to him as a Fish and guards him on an ark during the deluge, and makes him Vaivasvata Manu at the beginning of the next aeon.

**SAUBHA.‚Äî**King Salva; Saubhais the name of his capital which he could move at his will; is killed by Krishna.

**SAUNAKA.‚Äî**A Brahmin sage who performs sacrifice in the forest of Naimisa. It was to him and the others who assemble at his sacrifice that Suta recites all the Puranas.

**SIDDHAS.‚Äî**A class of semi-divine beings.

**SITA.‚Äî**Wife of Rama; daughter of king Janaka; an incarnation of Goddess Lakshmi; see the Ramayana; Vaideharajaduhita.

**SIVA.‚Äî**One of the Trinity; other names: Girisa, Sadasiva, Mahadeva, Vrishanka, Bhava; saves the world by drinking the deadly poison which the milky ocean churned by the gods and demons throws out.

**SONITA.‚Äî**The capital city of Banasura.

** SRI.‚Äî**Goddess Lakshmi who rises out of the milky ocean during its churning by the gods and the demons; chooses Lord Hari as Her Lord; the Goddess of wealth and fortune; other names: Rama, Lakshmi.

** SRIDAMAN.‚Äî**A cowherd.

**SUKA.‚Äî**Son of sage Vyasa; learnt the Bharata and all the Puranas from Vyasa; realised Brahman even as a boy; narrates the Bhagavata to Parikshit in seven days; also called Badarayani.

** SUNITHA.‚Äî**Wife of king Anga and mother of the terrible Vena.See footnote on p. 61.

** SUNITI.‚Äî**A wife of king wife of king Uttanapada; mother of Dhruva; neglected by her lord.

**SURAS.‚Äî**The gods; other names: Vibudhas; Divaukasas, Usriyas, Traivishtapeyas.

** SURASENA.‚Äî**A Yadu chief of Mathura; father of Vasudeva; grandfather of Krishna.

** SURASENAS.‚Äî**A. tribe related to the Yadavas.

**SURPANAKHI.‚Äî**Ademoness; sister sister of Ravana; disfigured by Lakshmana; sows the seed for the war between Rama and Ravana; see the Ramayana.

**SURUCHI.‚Äî**A wife of king Uttanapada; a favourite of her lord; mother of Uttama.

** SUTA.‚Äî**The minstrel who who recites recites the Puranas and the epic Mahabharata to sage Saunaka and others, assembled during the former’s sacrifice at Naimisa Son of Romaharshana, hence called Raumaharshani. His proper name is Ugrasravas.

**SVARGA.‚Äî**The heavens of which Indra is the lord; other names: Trinaka, Trivish- tapa, Nakaprishtha.

**SYAMANTAPANCHAKA.‚Äî**A place place in in the battle-field of Kurukshetra; here Parasurama created pools of blood by annihilating twenty-one generations of Kshatriyas.

**TAKSHAKA.‚Äî**A great serpent which, as a result of the curse of the son of a sage, stings king Parikshit.

**TARKSHYA.‚Äî**Father of Garuda, the vehicle of Lord Hari.

**TOSALAKA‚Äî**A wrestler in wrestler in the employ of king Kamsa.

** TRIKUTA‚Äî**A mountain on which the elephant king, Gajendra lived.

**TRINAVARTA.‚Äî**A demon friend of Kamsa who, as a whirlwind, tries to carry off baby Krishna, and dies in the attempt.

** TRIVIKRAMA.‚Äî**he gigantic form of the Lord, with which He bestrides the whole universe in three steps; also called Urukrama.

** TVASHTA.‚Äî**An architect of the gods; son of Kasyapa and Aditi; his wife was Rachana, belonging to the demons; father of Visvarupa who acts as the priest of the gods for some time and is killed by Indra.

** UCCHAISSRAVAS.‚Äî**A white horse that rises out of the milky ocean and which Indra takes for himself.

** UDDHAVA.‚Äî**A friend, devotee and counsellor of Krishna is sent by Krishna with a message to the inhabitants of Nanda’s hamlet; before His passage to his abode, the Lord discourses to him; retires to Badarikasrama and attains salvation.

** UGRASENA.‚Äî**A Yadu chief; rules at Mathura; son of Ahuka; brother of Devaka. the father of Devaki; Kamsa imprisons him and usurps the throne; Krishna reinstalls him after killing Kamsa.

** USANAS.‚Äî**The preceptor of the demons, the Asuras other names: Kavya (also Kavi).

** USHA.‚Äî**Daughter of Banasura; marries Aniruddha, grandson of Krishna.

**UTTARA.‚Äî**A king; father of Iravati,queen of Parikshit.

**UTTANAPADA.‚Äî**A son of Manu; see footnote on p. 32; father of Dhruva; has two wives, Suniti and Suruchi; Suruchi; is endowed with an element of the Lord.

**VACHASPATI.‚Äî**The preceptor of the gods; disappears from heaven being slighted by Indra once; in once; in his absence, Vritra, the Asura, captures Indra’s capital; other name: Brihaspati.

**VAMANA.‚Äî**The dwarf Brahmacharin-form which the Lord takes to subdue Bali, king of the demons; as a son of Kasyapa, Vamana becomes a brother of Indra.

** VARAHA.‚Äî**Also Adi Varaha, the primaeval Boar. The first of the Lord’s incarna- tions; lifts the earth out of the waters, where He kills also the demon named Hiranyaksha; also referred to as Kroda.

**VARUNA.‚Äî**The god of the waters and the Lord of the West.

** VARUNI.‚Äî**Wine; rises out of the milky ocean when it was churned; claimed by the demons.

**VASUDEVA.‚Äî**Of the Yadu race; son of Sura; brother of Kunti, the mother of the first three Pandavas; marries Devaki, daughter of Devaka, and sister of Kamsa; father of Balarama and Krishna; also called Sauri, Anakadundubhi and Surasuta.

**VASAVI.‚Äî**A name of Satyavati; so called because of her being the daughte: of Vasu, that is Uparichara Vasu; mother of Vyasa; wife of king Santanu.

**VASUKI.‚Äî**A great serpent who is used as the rope when the gods and the demons churn the milky ocean; referred to as Nagaraja also.

**VATSA.‚Äî**A demon who desires to kill Krishna, taking the form of a calf; Krishna kills him.

** VAYU.‚Äî**The Wind-god.

**VENA.‚Äî**Descendant of Dhruva; a tyrant. who is cursed to death by sages and Brahmins. See footnote on p. 61

** VISHNUYASAS.‚Äî**The Brahmin of Sambhala village, whose son the future Avatara of the Lord (Kalki) will be.

** VISVAKARMAN.‚Äî**The architect of the gods; makes the Vajra or thunderbolt for Indra out of sage Dadhichi’s bones, to kill Vritrasura.

** VISVARUPA.‚Äî**A Brahmin; sonof Tvashta; hence called Tvashtra; sought by Indra during the absence of Brihaspati; acts as Indra’s priest, but is slain by Indra for his partiality for the Asuras to whom he is related through his mother.

**VRAJA.‚Äî**The hamlet of Nanua, Nanua, where Krishna spends his boyhood; also called Gokula; referred to also as Nandavraja and Nandagokula (Nanda’s hamlet).

**VRAJAUKAS.‚Äî**The inhabitants of the Vraja, the hamlet of Nanda.

**VRISHABHA.‚Äî**A cowherd.

**VRITRA.‚Äî**The evil spirit created by Tvashta in his sacrificial fire, to kill Indra who murdered Visvarupa, the son of Tvashta; also referred to as Tvashtra, son of Tvashta.

**VYASA.‚Äî**The original composer of the Bhagavata and other Puranas and the Bharata father of Suka, who recites the Bhagavata to king Parikshit; a manifestation of the Lord; also called Badarayana and Krishna.

**YADUS.‚Äî**The race to which to which Vasudeva, Kamsa and Krishna belong; also Yadavas; they perish perish in a mutual fight after a carouse.

**YAKSHAS.‚Äî**A class of semi-divine beings.

**YAMA.‚Äî**The god of death; his capital is called Samyamani; hence he is referred to as Samyamanipati (Lord of Samyamani); also called Dandapani.

**YAMUNA.‚Äî**The Jumna; Dhruva practises austerities on its banks; scene of Krishna’s boyhood sport; also called Kalindi.

** YASODA‚Äî**Wife of the cowherd chief, Nanda; foster-mother of Krishna; Yoga Maya appears as her daughter.

**YUDHISHTHIRA.‚Äî**The eldest of the five Pandavas, the sons of the aunt of Krishna; grandfather of king Parikshit to whom the Bhagavata is narrated;also called Ajatasatru.
